Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Qada for Missed Prayers Due to Unconsciousness
Ruling with proof and cross-madhhab comparison

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for prayers missed due to unconsciousness and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
Unconsciousness waives qada for many prayers but requires it for few — a middle path to avoid hardship.

This lesson addresses a specific case of missed prayers: those caused by unconsciousness. The Hanafi school takes a middle position between two extremes: some schools require qada for all missed prayers regardless of the excuse; others waive qada entirely if unconsciousness covers even one full prayer time. The Hanafi ruling balances the principle of legal obligation with the avoidance of hardship, using istihsan (juristic preference) to modify the strict analogy (qiyas).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is making up (qada) obligatory prayers missed due to unconsciousness. According to the Hanafi school, if unconsciousness covers five prayers or fewer, qada is wajib; if it covers more than five prayers, qada is not wajib.
This is the mufta bihi position found in the Hidayah and other core texts.
2
Understand the qiyas position
Under pure analogical reasoning (qiyas), unconsciousness is like madness: it causes total incapacity. If a person misses even one full prayer time due to madness, qada is waived. By analogy, the same should apply to unconsciousness, meaning no qada at all.
The qiyas is based on the shared illa of incapacity ('ajz).
3
Understand the istihsan reasoning
Istihsan departs from qiyas to avoid hardship. If the unconsciousness is brief (five prayers or less), requiring qada imposes little hardship; if prolonged, the burden becomes excessive. The principle of raf' al-haraj (removal of hardship) justifies this departure.
The Dalil for raf' al-haraj is Quran 22:78.
4
Compare with other schools
The Malikis and Shafi'is follow the qiyas (no qada at all if even one full time is missed). The Hanbalis require qada for all missed prayers, comparing unconsciousness to illness. The Hanafi position is thus a middle path.
This thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is significant for fatwa.

ومن اغمى عليه خمس صلوات او دونها قضى وان كان اكثر من ذلك لم يقض وهذا استحسانا والقياس ان لا قضاء عليه اذا استوعب الاغماء وقت صلوة كامل لتحقق العجز فشبه الجنون وجه الاستحسان ان المدة اذا طالت كثرت الفوائت فيحرج فى الاداء و اذا قصرت قلت فلا حرج والكثير ان تزيد على يوم وليلة لانه يدخل في حد التكرار والجنون كالاغماء كذا ذكره ابوسليمان بخلاف النوم لان امتداده نادر فيلحق بالقاصر ثم الزيادة تعتبر من حيث الاوقات عند محمد لان التكرار يتحقق به وعندهما من حيث الساعات وهو الماثور عن علي و ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما والله اعلم بالصواب

حنابلہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اغماء ایک قسم کا مرض ہے اور مرض میں جس قدر نمازیں فوت ہو جائیں ان کی قضاء واجب ہوتی ہے لہذا اس صورت میں بھی قضاء واجب ہوگی خواہ فوت شدہ نمازیں کثیر ہی کیوں نہ ہوں۔ امام مالک اور امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب اغماء نے نماز کا پورا وقت گھیر لیا تو عجز متحقق ہو گیا اور بوجہ بعض جنون کے مشابہ ہو گیا پس بعض حضرات کے نزدیک جس طرح ایک نماز کے پورے وقت کا جنون قضاء واجب نہیں کرتا اسی طرح اغماء کی صورت میں بھی قضاء واجب نہ ہوگی۔

استحسان جو علماء احناف کی دلیل ہے یہ ہے کہ مدت اغماء جب دراز ہو جائے گی تو فوت شدہ نمازیں کثیر ہو جائیں گی۔ اب اگر ان کثیرہ کی قضاء کا حکم دیا جائے گا تو وہ شخص حرج میں پڑ جائے اور چونکہ شریعت اسلام میں حرج کو دور کیا گیا ہے اس لئے ان فوائت کثیرہ کی قضاء واجب نہیں کی گئی۔ اور اگر مدت اغماء کم ہے تو فوت شدہ نمازیں قلیل ہوں گی اور فوائت قلیلہ کی قضاء کرنے میں چونکہ کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اس لئے فوائت قلیلہ کی قضاء کا حکم دیا گیا ہے احناف کی دلیل کو اس طرح بھی بیان کیا جاسکتا ہے کہ عذر تین طرح کے ہیں اول عذر مثل بچپن تو یہ بالاجماع مانع فرضیت ہے دوم قاصر جیسے نیند کہ وہ بالاتفاق مانع نہیں حتی کہ نیند کی وجہ سے اگر نماز فوت ہوگئی تو اس کی قضا واجب ہے سوم جو درمیانی درجہ پر ہے جنون اور اغماء پر اگر یہ دراز ہو جائیں تو ممتد کے ساتھ لاحق ہوں گے حتی کہ قضاء ساقط ہو جائے اور اگر کم ہوں تو قاصر کے ساتھ لاحق ہونگے حتی کہ قضاء واجب ہوگی۔ واضح ہو کہ کثرت کی حد یہ ہے کہ فوت شدہ نمازیں ایک رات دن سے بڑھ جائیں حتی کہ چھٹی نماز کا وقت نکل جائے کیونکہ جب چھٹی نماز کا وقت نکل گیا تو نمازوں میں تکرار شروع ہو گیا اور تکرار کے بعد کثرت کا ظاہر ہونا لازم ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے "والجنون كالاغماء" سے امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب دیا ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اغماء ان کے مانند نہیں بلکہ جنون اغماء کے مانند ہے یعنی جنون اگر پانچ نمازوں سے زائد رہا تو قضاء ساقط ہوگی اور اگر کم ہے تو ساقط نہ ہو گی ۔ ابوسلیمان نے یہی ذکر کیا ہے اس کے برخلاف نیند کہ اگر وہ زائد بھی ہو تب بھی قضاء ساقط نہ ہوگی کیونکہ نیند کا ممتد ہونا نادر ہے لہذا اس کو قاصر کے ساتھ لاحق کیا جائے گا نہ کہ عذر ممتد کے ساتھ ۔

علماء احناف اس بات پر متفق ہیں کہ کثیر کی حد یہ ہے کہ فوت شدہ نمازیں ایک رات دن سے بڑھ جائیں لیکن اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ یہ حد من حیث الاوقات معتبر ہے یا من حیث الساعات معتبر ہے؟ امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ من حیث الاوقات معتبر ہے یعنی اگر چھ نمازیں فوت ہوگئیں اور چھٹی نماز کا وقت گذر گیا تو کثرت ثابت ہو جائے گی اور کثرت فوائت کی وجہ سے قضاء واجب نہ ہوگی اور اگر چھٹی نماز کا وقت نہیں گذرا بلکہ کچھ ساعتیں گذری ہیں تو امام محمد کے نزدیک کثرت ثابت نہ ہوگی اور اس کے ذمہ سے قضاء ساقط نہ ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے امام محمد کی دلیل ذکر کرتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ تکرار چھ نمازوں کے فوت ہونے سے ہی متحقق ہوگا اور چھ نمازوں کا فوت ہونا عین موجب حرج ہے جو قضاء کو ساقط کرنے والا ہے لہذا کثرت کی تحدید میں نمازوں کا فوت ہونا ہی معتبر ہے شیخین نے کہا ہے کہ کثرت میں ساعات معتبر ہیں نہ کہ اوقات یعنی ایک دن رات سے اگر ایک دو ساعت بھی زیادہ ہوگئی تو کثرت ثابت ہو جائے گی یہی علی اور حضرت عبداللہ بن عمر رضی اللہ عنہم سے منقول ہے۔ شمر اختلاف اس صورت میں ظاہر ہوگا کہ ایک شخص پر چاشت کے وقت بے ہوشی طاری ہوگئی پھر اگلے دن زوال سے ایک ساعت پہلے افاقہ ہو گیا (ہوش آ گیا) تو یہ ساعات کے اعتبار سے ایک دن رات سے [نقص؟] ہے شیخین کے نزدیک اس پر قضاء واجب نہ ہوگی اور امام محمد کے نزدیک اس پر قضاء واجب ہوگی کیونکہ اس صورت میں نمازوں کے [؟]
Chapter on the Prayer of the Sick. ... More tranquility, but if exiting the boat is impossible yet he did not exit and prayed in the boat, it is permissible. The author of Hidayah says: The dispute about permission or impermissibility of praying sitting without excuse concerns a boat that is tied to the shore, not one moving; a boat tied to the shore is like the bank of the river, i.e., just as praying sitting without excuse on the ground by the riverbank is not permissible, similarly in a tied boat praying sitting without excuse is not permissible. The correct view is this. If unconsciousness covers five prayers or less, they are made up; if more than that, not. And [the text]: 'Whoever is unconscious for five prayers or less, he makes them up; if it is more than that, he does not make them up. This is according to istihsan. The qiyas would be that there is no qada upon him when unconsciousness covers the entire time of one prayer because incapacity is realized, so it resembles madness. The basis of istihsan is that when the period is long, the missed prayers become many, so there would be hardship in performing them; when it is short, they are few, so no hardship. Many (kathir) means exceeding a day and a night, because it enters the limit of repetition. Madness is like unconsciousness; thus Abu Sulayman mentioned it. Unlike sleep, because its prolongation is rare, so it is attached to the minor excuse. Then the increase in number is considered by the times (awqat) according to Muhammad, because repetition is realized by that; and according to the two (Shaykhayn), by the hours (sa'at). This is what is narrated from Ali and Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them. And Allah knows best.' Translation: And the one upon whom unconsciousness persists for five prayers or less, he makes them up; if more than that, he does not make them up. This is istihsan. Qiyas is that no qada is due when unconsciousness covers the entire time of one prayer because incapacity is realized, so unconsciousness resembles madness. The reason for istihsan is that when the period of unconsciousness is long, the missed prayers become many, so there would be hardship in making them up; when the period is short, they are few, so no hardship. Kathir (many) means the missed prayers exceed one day and night, because they enter the limit of repetition. Madness is like unconsciousness; similarly Abu Sulayman mentioned. Unlike sleep, because its prolongation is rare, so sleep is attached to the minor excuse. Then increase and kathir according to Imam Muhammad are considered by the number of prayer times (awqat) because repetition is realized by that; according to the Shaykhayn, it is considered by hours. This is narrated from Ali and Ibn Umar. Allah knows best. Explanation: If a person remains unconscious for more than five prayers, making them up is not obligatory; this ruling is by istihsan. Qiyas would be that if unconsciousness covers the entire time of one prayer, no qada is due. According to Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and the Hanbalis, making up missed prayers is obligatory even if a thousand prayers. The Hanbalis say regardless of few or many, qada is obligatory; Malik and Shafi'i say if unconsciousness covers the entire time of one prayer, even if one prayer is missed, qada is not obligatory. Our scholars (Hanafis) took a middle path: if the missed prayers are few, qada is obligatory; if many, qada is not obligatory. Hanbali proof: unconsciousness is a type of illness, and prayers missed due to illness must be made up regardless of number. Maliki and Shafi'i proof: when unconsciousness covers the full time of a prayer, incapacity is realized, resembling madness, so no qada. Hanafi proof (istihsan): if the period is long, many prayers are missed, causing hardship; since hardship is removed in Islam, qada for many is waived; if short, few prayers, no hardship, so qada is obligatory. Another expression: Excuses are three types: (1) like childhood, which prevents obligation by consensus; (2) minor (qasir) like sleep, which does not prevent obligation; (3) intermediate like madness and unconsciousness: if prolonged, they attach to the extended type, so qada is waived; if short, they attach to the minor type, so qada is obligatory. The limit of kathir is that missed prayers exceed a day and night such that the sixth prayer time passes; when the sixth prayer time passes, repetition begins, and kathir necessarily appears. The author of Hidayah replied to the Maliki/Shafi'i analogy with 'and madness is like unconsciousness': the reply is that unconsciousness is not like their analogy; rather, madness is like unconsciousness—if madness lasts more than five prayers, qada is waived; if less, not waived. Abu Sulayman mentioned this. Unlike sleep: even if prolonged, qada is not waived because its prolongation is rare; thus it is attached to the minor excuse, not the extended one. Hanafi scholars agree that the limit of kathir is that missed prayers exceed a day and night, but there is a difference: is this limit considered by the number of prayer times (awqat) or by hours? Imam Muhammad said by prayer times: if six prayers are missed and the sixth prayer time has passed, kathir is established and no qada; if the sixth time has not passed but some hours have passed, then according to Imam Muhammad, kathir is not established and qada is not waived. The author of Hidayah mentions Imam Muhammad's proof: repetition is realized only by missing six prayers, and missing six prayers is precisely what causes hardship which calls for waiving qada, so the limit of kathir is based on missing prayers themselves. The Shaykhayn said that kathir is determined by hours, not prayer times: if the duration exceeds a day and night by even one or two hours, kathir is established. This is narrated from Ali and Ibn Umar. The difference appears in this case: a person becomes unconscious at the time of chasht (forenoon) and then regains consciousness an hour before noon the next day; then by hours it exceeds a day and night, so according to the Shaykhayn, no qada; according to Imam Muhammad, qada is obligatory because in this case the prayers... [incomplete]
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage from 'Ashraf al-Hidayah' is a commentary on the chapter of prayer for the sick. It primarily addresses the ruling on making up (qada) obligatory prayers missed due to unconsciousness (ighma). The text begins with a brief discussion about praying in a boat while sitting without excuse, then moves to the core issue. The key ruling, stated in the Arabic matn of al-Hidayah, is: if a person is unconscious for five prayers or fewer, they must be made up; if more than five, no qada is required. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference), which is a departure from qiyas (analogy). Under pure qiyas, since unconsciousness constitutes a genuine incapacity analogous to madness, one would not owe qada even for a single prayer whose entire time was missed. However, the Hanafi school gives weight to the principle of avoiding hardship (raf' al-haraj): if unconsciousness is brief (five prayers or less), the burden of making them up is minor; if it is prolonged, requiring qada for many prayers would cause excessive hardship, so it is waived. The text then contrasts the Hanafi position with other schools: the Hanbalis require qada regardless of number; the Malikis and Shafi'is follow the qiyas view, requiring no qada at all if unconsciousness covers even one full prayer time. The Hanafi response, via istihsan, is a middle path. The passage further delves into the definition of 'many' (kathir), which is the threshold for waiving qada. The agreed-upon standard is that kathir means the missed prayers exceed a day and night (i.e., six prayers). However, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (dispute) between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) on how to measure this: by the number of prayer times (awqat) or by the total hours (sa'at). Imam Muhammad considers the actual passage of six prayer times (e.g., if the sixth prayer time has passed), while the Shaykhayn consider the total duration exceeding 24 hours by any amount. This difference has practical consequences in precise calculation. The text ends with an example but cuts off, though the core positions are clear.

Key Terms
إغماء (ighmā'): Unconsciousness; a state in which a person is unaware of surroundings and unable to perform acts of worship.
قضاء (qaḍā'): Making up a missed obligatory act of worship after its prescribed time.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; departing from strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more suitable ruling based on a stronger evidence or principle.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared effective cause ('illa).
كثير (kathīr): Many; the threshold for missed prayers beyond which qada is waived. Defined as exceeding one day and night (six prayers).
قليل (qalīl): Few; five prayers or less, for which qada is wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person remains unconscious for the times of six obligatory prayers, what is the ruling on making them up?
A) Qada is wajib for all six.
B) Qada is not wajib because the number exceeds five.
C) Qada is wajib only if the total hours exceed 24.
D) Qada is not wajib because unconsciousness waives all qada.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school waives qada for many missed prayers due to prolonged unconsciousness to avoid hardship, but requires it for few, balancing obligation with ease.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Qada for Missed Prayers During Prolonged Fainting: The Hanafi Distinction
Inter-madhhab dispute with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qada for prayers missed due to fainting, distinguish between short and prolonged duration, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the Shaykhayn.

Core Idea
Prolonged fainting waives qada; short fainting requires it, based on istihsan to remove hardship.

The obligation to make up missed prayers after fainting might seem straightforward, but the Hanafi school makes a nuanced distinction based on duration. This lesson explores why fainting is treated differently from ordinary illness or sleep, and how the Hanafi jurists used istihsan to avoid hardship. We will also examine the intra-madhhab disagreement on the exact threshold for 'many' missed prayers.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two-tier ruling: if fainting is short (≤5 prayers or ≤24 hours), qada is wajib; if prolonged (>5 prayers or >24 hours), qada is waived.
This applies to both ighma (fainting) and junun (insanity) by analogy.
2
Identify opposing schools and their proofs
The Hanbalis analogize fainting to illness, requiring qada for all missed prayers. The Malikis and Shafi'is analogize fainting to insanity, waiving qada entirely.
Each school uses qiyas (analogy) but with different asl (original case).
3
Analyse the Hanafi response using istihsan
The Hanafis argue that fainting is neither like ordinary illness (which does not remove consciousness) nor always like insanity. Instead, they introduce istihsan based on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj). They classify excuses into three categories: comprehensive (like childhood), restrictive (like sleep), and intermediate (fainting/insanity). The intermediate becomes comprehensive if prolonged, restrictive if short.
Istihsan overrides qiyas in this case due to the strong consideration of hardship.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on the definition of 'many'
Imam Muhammad defines 'many' by prayer times: if the sixth prayer's time enters (i.e., more than five prayers missed), kathrat is established. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) define it by hours: if fainting exceeds 24 hours plus an extra hour, kathrat is established.
The practical difference emerges in borderline cases, e.g., fainting from Duha to just before noon the next day.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
For the Hanbali, all fainting requires qada; for Maliki/Shafi'i, none requires qada; for Hanafi, it depends on duration. Within Hanafi, the mufta bihi view is Imam Muhammad's, so the threshold is the passing of the sixth prayer's time.
This ruling significantly affects people with medical conditions causing prolonged unconsciousness.

Chapter on the prayer of the sick. The Hanbalis' proof is that fainting is a type of illness, and within illness, whatever prayers are missed, their qada is obligatory. Therefore, in this case too, qada is obligatory, even if the missed prayers are many. The proof of Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i is that when fainting covers the entire time of prayer, then the person becomes unconscious, and according to some, it resembles insanity. So, according to some scholars, just as insanity for the time of one prayer does not obligate qada, similarly in the case of fainting, qada will not be obligatory. As for istihsan, which is the proof of the Hanafi scholars, it is that when the duration of fainting becomes prolonged, the missed prayers become many. Now if qada of these many prayers is commanded, then the person will fall into hardship, and since hardship is removed in the Islamic law, therefore qada of these missed prayers is not made obligatory. And if the duration of fainting is short, then the missed prayers are few, and since there is no difficulty in performing qada of few missed prayers, therefore qada of few missed prayers is commanded. The Hanafi proof can also be expressed as follows: Excuses are of three types: (1) comprehensive such as childhood, which prevents obligation by consensus; (2) restrictive such as sleep, which does not prevent obligation by consensus, so much so that if a prayer is missed due to sleep, its qada is obligatory; (3) that which is of an intermediate level, such as insanity and fainting - if these become prolonged, they are attached to the prolonged excuse, so qada falls, but if they are short, they are attached to the restrictive, so qada is obligatory. It is clear that the limit of "many" is that the missed prayers exceed one night and day, such that the time for the sixth prayer passes, because when the sixth time passes, repetition of prayers begins, and after repetition, the appearance of many is inevitable. The author of Al-Hidayah answered the analogy of Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i with the words "and insanity is like fainting". The conclusion of the answer is that fainting is not like insanity; rather insanity is like fainting, i.e., if insanity exceeds five prayers, qada falls, and if it is less, it does not fall. This is what is mentioned by [some]. In contrast, sleep, even if it is prolonged, qada does not fall because sleep's being prolonged is rare, so it is attached to the restrictive excuse, not the prolonged excuse. The Hanafi scholars agree that the limit of "many" is that the missed prayers exceed one night and day. But there is a difference of opinion as to whether this is considered by prayer times or by hours. Imam Muhammad said: consideration is by prayer times, meaning that even if six prayers are missed and the time for the sixth prayer passes, kathrat (many) is established, and due to the kathrat of missed prayers, qada is not obligatory. And if the time for the sixth prayer has not passed, but only some hours have passed, then according to Imam Muhammad, kathrat is not established and qada is not waived from his responsibility. The author [of Al-Hidayah] mentioned Imam Muhammad's proof saying: repetition occurs only by missing six prayers, and missing six prayers leads to hardship, which waives qada; therefore, in the definition of kathrat, the missing of prayers is what is considered. The Shaykhayn said: in kathrat, hours are considered, not times, i.e., if even one or two hours more than one night and day pass, then kathrat is established. This is also transmitted from [someone] and from Abdullah ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). The difference will appear in this case: a person becomes unconscious at the time of Duha, then the next day he regains consciousness one hour before noon. So this, by consideration of hours, is [more than] one night and day? Hence according to Shaykhayn, qada will not be obligatory for him, and according to Imam Muhammad, qada will be obligatory for him, because in this case the prayers...
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the obligation of making up prayers missed due to prolonged fainting (ighma) or insanity (junun). The Hanbalis analogize fainting to ordinary illness, requiring qada for all missed prayers. Malik and Shafi'i analogize fainting to insanity, arguing that since insanity for a short period does not require qada, fainting also does not. The Hanafi school, using istihsan, distinguishes between short and long durations: if fainting lasts less than one day and night (i.e., missing up to five prayers), qada is obligatory; if it exceeds five prayers (sixth prayer's time enters), qada is waived due to hardship. The text further defines the limit of 'kathir' (many) and presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Imam Muhammad considers prayer times (whether five prayers are exceeded), while the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) consider total hours (whether the fainting exceeds 24 hours plus an extra hour or two). The example of a person fainting at Duha and waking one hour before noon the next day illustrates the difference. The commentary follows the author's order by first presenting the views of other schools, then the Hanafi position with its istihsan proof, then the internal Hanafi dispute. The teacher should note that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Imam Muhammad considering prayer times, as it is more precise and avoids unnecessary qada in many cases.

Key Terms
اغماء (ighmā’): Fainting or unconsciousness that prevents awareness and performance of acts of worship.
جنون (junūn): Insanity or severe mental disorder that removes legal responsibility.
قضاء (qaḍā’): Making up a missed obligation after its designated time.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Equity or juristic preference that overrides analogy due to a stronger consideration.
حرج (ḥaraj): Hardship or difficulty that the law seeks to remove.
کثیر (kathīr): A large number; in this context, more than five prayers or more than one day and night of unconsciousness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school, if a person faints for 12 hours and misses 4 prayers, are they required to make up those prayers?
A) No, because any fainting waives qada.
B) Yes, because they missed fewer than five prayers and the fainting was short.
C) No, because fainting is like insanity and insanity waives qada.
D) Yes, because all missed prayers must be made up regardless.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to waive qada for prolonged fainting to avoid hardship, but requires qada for short fainting, with the mufta bihi view considering prayer times.

The Fourteen Prostrations of Recitation: A Hanafi Memorization List
Hanafi list of fourteen sajda tilawa verses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite the fourteen surahs containing sajda al-tilawa and identify the two special rulings regarding the second prostration in al-Hajj and the verse in Ha Meem al-Sajda.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school counts fourteen prostrations of recitation, based on the Mushaf of Uthman, with a second prostration in al-Hajj for prayer and the verse in Ha Meem identified by the phrase 'la yas'amun'.

This passage from Al-Quduri provides the definitive Hanafi list of verses where prostration is wajib upon recitation or hearing. Understanding this list is essential for fulfilling a wajib act in salah. The passage also clarifies two special cases that often cause confusion: the second prostration in Surah al-Hajj and the exact wording of the prostration verse in Surah Ha Meem al-Sajda.

Guided Path
1
Identify the total number and authority
The Hanafi school states there are exactly fourteen prostrations in the Quran. This count is taken from the Mushaf of Uthman and transmitted by Imam al-Quduri. Recognize that this is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
Other schools may count fifteen; the Hanafi position is based on the standard mushaf.
2
Memorize the fourteen surahs
List the surahs in order as given: al-A'raf, al-Ra'd, al-Nahl, Bani Isra'il, Maryam, first in al-Hajj, al-Furqan, al-Naml, al-Ma'rif (al-Sajda), Sad, Ha Meem al-Sajda, al-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, al-'Alaq (Iqra'). Learn them sequentially.
The second prostration in al-Hajj is not counted as a separate sajda tilawa; it is for prayer.
3
Understand the two special rulings
First, the second prostration in Surah al-Hajj is specifically for prayer (i.e., it is performed during salah, not as a standalone tilawa). Second, in Ha Meem al-Sajda, the prostration verse is the one containing the phrase 'la yas'amun' (they do not get weary), based on the precautionary opinion of Umar.
The ruling for the second sajda in Hajj indicates that it is not part of the list of fourteen recitation prostrations.
4
Practice with verse identification
If you have a Quran, locate each verse to reinforce memorization. For Ha Meem al-Sajda, look for the verse that includes 'la yas'amun'. This is a precaution to ensure the correct prostration.

تشریح مناسب بات یہ تھی کہ سجدہ تلاوت کو سجدہ سہو کے فورا بعد ذکر کیا جاتا اس لئے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک بجد ہے مگر اکو مریض کی نماز عارض سماوی کی وجہ سے ہے اور کہو بھی عارض سماوی سے ہوتا ہے اس مناسبت کی وجہ سے سجدہ سہو کے بعد لو امر الان بیان کیا گیا ہے پس جب اس مناسبت کی وجہ سے سجدہ سہو کے بعد صلاوہ مریض بیان کیا گیا ہے تو سجدہ تلاوت کا بیان لا ز مامور ہو جائے گا۔ سجدہ تلاوت میں حکم کی اضافت سب کی طرف کی گئی ہے کیونکہ تلاوت کے سجدہ کا سبب تلاوت ہی ہے لیکن اگر کوئی اعتراضایں۔ کہ تلاوت کے علاوہ سماع بھی سجدہ کا سبب ہے تو اس طرح کہنا چاہئے تھا کہ مسجود التلاوت والسماع اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ : جس طرح سجدہ کا سبب ہے اسی طرح سماع کا بھی سبب ہے، پس تلاوت کا ذکر من وجہ سماع کے ذکر کو بھی مشتمل ہے اس لئے تلاوت ۔ ذکر پر اکتفاء کیا گیا ہے۔
قرآن کریم میں کل کتنے سجدے ہیں اور کون کون سی سورت میں ہیں
قال سجود التلاوة فى القرآن اربعة عشر فى آخر الاعراف وفى الرعد والنحل و بنی اسرائیل و مرم والاولى من الحج والفرقان والنمل و الم تنزيل و ص و حم السجدة والنجم واذا السماء انشقت واقرأكا كتب في مصحف عثمان وهو المعتمد والسجدة الثانية في الحج للصلوة عندنا و موضع السجدة في حر السجدة عند قوله لا يسأمون فى قول عمر و هو الماخوذ للاحتياط
ترجمہ صاحبقدوری نے کہا کہ قرآن میں تلاوت کے سجدے چودہ ہیں سورہ اعراف کے آخر میں سورہ رعد میں سورہ شکل میں کو نبی اسرائیل میں سورۃ مریم میں پہلا سجدہ سورہ حج میں، سورۂ فرقان میں سورہ نمل میں سورۃ الم تنزیل میں سور کص میں سورة تم الجدار سورۃ النجم میں سورۃ اذا السماء انشقت مین اور سورۃ اتر آئیں اسی طرح حضرت عثمان کے مصحف میں لکھا ہوا ہے اور وہی معتمد ہے سورہ حج میں دوسرا سجدہ ہمارے نزدیک نماز کے لئے ہے۔ اور حم السجدہ میں موضع سجدہ حضرت عمر کے قول کے مطابق لابساموں اور یہی قول بنظر احتیاط لیا گیا ہے۔
تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ قرآن پاک میں آیات سجدہ چودہ ہیں، (1) سورۃ اعراف کے آخر میں، إِنَّ الَّذِينَ عِندَ رَبِّكَ لَا يَسْتَكْبِرُونَ عَنْ عِبَادَتِهِ وَيُسَبِّحُوْنَهُ وَلَهُ يَسْجُدُونَ (په) (۲) سورہ رعد میں ہے، وَلِلَّهِ مَنْ فِى السَّمَوتِ وَالْأَرْضِ طَوْعًا وَ كَرْهًا وَ ظِلَالُهُمْ بِالْغُدُةِ وَالْأَصَالِ : ( و) (۳) سور فحل میں ہے، يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُمُ مِّنْ فَوْقِهِمْ وَ يَفْعَلُونَ مَا يُؤْمَرُوْنَ - سورہ بنی اسرائیل میں ہے، وَيَخِرُّونَ لِلاذْقَانِ يَبْكُونَ وَيَزِيدُهُم خُشُوعًا -
Chapter on the prostration of recitation. Translation: This is about the prostration of recitation. Commentary: The appropriate thing was that the prostration of recitation should be mentioned immediately after the prostration of forgetfulness, because each of these two is a prostration, but the prayer of the sick is due to a heavenly affliction, and forgetfulness also occurs due to a heavenly affliction. Due to this suitability, after the prostration of forgetfulness, the prayer of the sick was mentioned. So since the prayer of the sick was mentioned after the prostration of forgetfulness due to this suitability, the statement of the prostration of recitation becomes necessary. In the prostration of recitation, the ruling is attributed to recitation (tilawa) because the cause of the prostration of recitation is recitation itself. But if someone objects that besides recitation, hearing (sama') is also a cause of prostration, then it should have been said 'the prostration of recitation and hearing'. The answer is that just as recitation is a cause, similarly hearing is also a cause. So the mention of recitation, in one sense, includes the mention of hearing. Therefore, reliance on the mention of recitation suffices. How many prostrations are in the Quran and in which surahs? He said: The prostrations of recitation in the Quran are fourteen: at the end of al-A'raf, in al-Ra'd, al-Nahl, Bani Isra'il, Maryam, the first in al-Hajj, al-Furqan, al-Naml, Alif Lam Meem Tanzil, Sad, Ha Meem al-Sajda, al-Najm, Idha al-Sama'u Inshaqqat, and Iqra', as written in the Mushaf of Uthman, and that is the relied-upon. And the second prostration in al-Hajj is for prayer according to us. And the place of prostration in Ha Meem al-Sajda is at His statement 'la yas'amun' according to the saying of Umar, and that is taken as a precaution. Translation: Imam al-Quduri said: The prostrations of recitation in the Quran are fourteen: at the end of Surah al-A'raf, in Surah al-Ra'd, in Surah Nahl, in Surah Bani Isra'il, in Surah Maryam, the first prostration in Surah al-Hajj, in Surah al-Furqan, in Surah al-Naml, in Surah Alim Lam Meem Tanzil, in Surah Sad, in Surah Ha Meem al-Sajda, in Surah al-Najm, in Surah Idha al-Sama'u Inshaqqat, and in Surah Iqra'. In this way it is written in the Mushaf of Uthman and it is the relied-upon. The second prostration in Surah al-Hajj, according to us, is for prayer. And the place of prostration in Ha Meem al-Sajda is at His statement 'la yas'amun' according to the saying of Umar, and this saying is taken as a precaution. Commentary: Imam al-Quduri said that in the Holy Quran there are fourteen verses of prostration: (1) At the end of Surah al-A'raf: إِنَّ الَّذِينَ عِندَ رَبِّكَ لَا يَسْتَكْبِرُونَ عَنْ عِبَادَتِهِ وَيُسَبِّحُوْنَهُ وَلَهُ يَسْجُدُونَ (2) In Surah al-Ra'd: وَلِلَّهِ مَنْ فِى السَّمَوتِ وَالْأَرْضِ طَوْعًا وَ كَرْهًا وَ ظِلَالُهُمْ بِالْغُدُةِ وَالْأَصَالِ (3) In Surah Nahl: يَخَافُونَ رَبَّهُمُ مِّنْ فَوْقِهِمْ وَ يَفْعَلُونَ مَا يُؤْمَرُوْنَ - In Surah Bani Isra'il: وَيَخِرُّونَ لِلاذْقَانِ يَبْكُونَ وَيَزِيدُهُم خُشُوعًا
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the chapter on sajda al-tilawa (prostration of recitation). It begins with a short discussion on why this chapter is placed after the prayer of the sick: both involve prostration, and both have a heavenly cause (forgetfulness and illness). The main content is a memorization anchor listing the fourteen prostrations in the Quran according to the Hanafi school, as stated by Imam al-Quduri and based on the Mushaf of Uthman. The list includes specific surahs: al-A'raf, al-Ra'd, al-Nahl, Bani Isra'il (al-Isra'), Maryam, the first in al-Hajj, al-Furqan, al-Naml, al-Ma'rif (al-Sajda), Sad, Ha Meem al-Sajda (Fussilat), al-Najm, al-Inshiqaq, and al-'Alaq (Iqra'). The passage also mentions two special rulings: (1) The second prostration in Surah al-Hajj is for prayer (i.e., it is performed during prayer, not as a separate recitation ?), (2) The prostration verse in Ha Meem al-Sajda is the verse containing the phrase 'la yas'amun' (they do not get weary), according to a narration from Umar, which is taken as a precaution to ensure the prostration is valid. The commentary then begins to list the actual verse texts but is incomplete. The teacher should explain that these fourteen are the ones on which the Hanafi school relies, and they are considered wajib to perform upon reciting or hearing them.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration in the Quran.
مصحف عثمان (muṣḥaf ʿUthmān): The standard copy of the Quran compiled by Caliph Uthman ibn Affan, which is the basis for the canonical text.
حر السجدة (ḥurr al-sajdah): The actual verse of prostration; the specific wording that triggers the prostration obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many prostrations of recitation are there in the Quran according to the Hanafi school?
A) Thirteen
B) Fourteen
C) Fifteen
D) Twelve

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school enumerates fourteen verses of prostration in the Quran, relying on the Mushaf of Uthman, with the unique identification that the second prostration in al-Hajj is for prayer and the verse in Ha Meem al-Sajda is the one containing 'la yas'amun'.

The Prostration of Recitation: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i on Surah al-Hajj and Sad
Enumeration of fourteen prostrations and dispute over al-Hajj and Sad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of prostrations in Surah al-Hajj and Sad, and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i evidence.

Core Idea
Only one prostration of recitation in al-Hajj; the second is for prayer.

The prostrations of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah) are a well-known feature of Quran recitation, but their number and location are not without scholarly disagreement. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position, which relies on the Mushaf of Uthman and the statements of Companions, and contrast it with the Shafi'i view regarding two key surahs: al-Hajj and Sad.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on the prostrations in al-Hajj and Sad
Identify what the Hanafi school concludes: the first prostration in al-Hajj is tilawah, the second is for prayer (salah); the prostration in Sad is tilawah.
Also note that the Hanafi list includes 14 prostrations.
2
State the Shafi'i position
Contrast with al-Shafi'i: both prostrations in al-Hajj are tilawah, and Sad is a prostration of thanksgiving (shukr), not tilawah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi evidence (dalil)
Examine the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar, which directly supports the Hanafi view, and the reliance on the Mushaf of Uthman.
Hanafi evidence is based on explicit Companion statements.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i evidence
Review the hadith of Uqbah ibn Amir for al-Hajj and the hadith about the repentance of a prophet for Sad.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafi school interprets the Shafi'i evidence: the Uqbah hadith is understood to mean one tilawah and one salah prostration; the Sad hadith does not negate its tilawah status.
This shows the Hanafi method of reconciling conflicting proofs.

Source Text

باب في سجدة التلاوة
قال سجود التلاوة فى القرآن اربعة عشر فى آخر الاعراف وفى الرعد والنحل و بني اسرائيل و مرم والاولى من الحج والفرقان والنمل و الم تنزيل و ص و حم السجدة والنجم واذا السماء انشقت واقرأ كا كتب في مصحف عثمان وهو المعتمد والسجدة الثانية في الحج للصلوة عندنا و موضع السجدة في حم السجدة عند قوله لا يسأمون في قول عمر و هو الماخوذ للاحتياط. والسجدة الثانيه في الحج اليه اشارة الخلاف: ان امام الشافعي عنده ايضا ايات السجدة اربعة عشر لكن عنده في الحج السجدتان كلتاهما سجدة تلاوة، وعندنا الاولى سجدة تلاوة والثانية سجدة الصلوة. وفي ص عندنا سجدة تلاوة وعند الشافعي سجدة شكر. دليلنا حديث ابن عباس وابن عمر: "سجدة التلاوة في الحج هي الاولى والثانية سجدة الصلوة". ودليل الشافعي حديث عقبة بن عامر: "فضلت الحج بسجدتين من لم يسجدهما فلم يقرأهما". وجوابنا: تاويله ان الاولى سجدة تلاوة والثانية سجدة الصلوة. وفي ص دليل الشافعي حديث: "انها توبة نبي".
Chapter on the prostration of recitation. He said: The prostrations of recitation in the Quran are fourteen: at the end of al-A'raf, in al-Ra'd, al-Nahl, Bani Isra'il, Maryam, the first of al-Hajj, al-Furqan, al-Naml, Alif Lam Mim Tanzil, Sad, Ha Mim al-Sajdah, al-Najm, Idha al-Sama'unshaqqat, and Iqra'. As written in the Mushaf of Uthman, and that is the relied-upon. And the second prostration in al-Hajj is for prayer according to us. And the place of prostration in Ha Mim al-Sajdah is at His saying 'la yas'amun' according to the saying of Umar, and that is taken for precaution. And the second prostration in al-Hajj indicates a point of difference: that Imam al-Shafi'i also has fourteen verses of prostration, but according to him both prostrations in al-Hajj are recitation prostrations, while according to us the first is a recitation prostration and the second is a prayer prostration. And in Sad, according to us it is a recitation prostration, according to al-Shafi'i it is a prostration of thanksgiving. Our evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar: 'The recitation prostration in al-Hajj is the first, and the second is the prostration of prayer.' And the evidence of al-Shafi'i is the hadith of Uqbah ibn Amir: 'Al-Hajj has been favored with two prostrations; whoever does not prostrate for them has not read them.' Our response: its interpretation is that the first is a recitation prostration and the second is a prayer prostration. And for Sad, the evidence of al-Shafi'i is the hadith: 'It is the repentance of a prophet.'
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the number and location of prostrations of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah). The author, from the Hanafi school, first lists the fourteen prostrations as recorded in the Mushaf of Uthman, which is the authoritative source. Then he addresses a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i concerning two specific prostrations: the second prostration in Surah al-Hajj and the prostration in Surah Sad. According to the Hanafis, Surah al-Hajj contains only one prostration of recitation (the first); the second prostration in that surah is the prostration of prayer (sajdat al-salah), not tilawah. As for Surah Sad, the Hanafis consider it a prostration of recitation, whereas al-Shafi'i considers it a prostration of thanksgiving (sajdat al-shukr). The Hanafi evidence comes from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar, who explicitly state that the second prostration in al-Hajj is for prayer. The Shafi'i evidence is a hadith from Uqbah ibn Amir: "Al-Hajj has been favored with two prostrations; whoever does not prostrate for them has not read them." The Hanafi response is to interpret the hadith as referring to one tilawah prostration and one salah prostration, not two tilawah prostrations. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of reconciling apparently conflicting evidence by understanding the context and considering the practice of the Companions. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is the one presented here, as it is based on the Mushaf of Uthman and the statements of the Companions.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): The prostration performed when reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration in the Quran.
مصحف عثمان (mushaf 'uthman): The standard codex of the Quran compiled during the caliphate of Uthman. Used as authoritative evidence for the number and location of prostrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many prostrations of recitation are in Surah al-Hajj?
A) Two prostrations of recitation
B) One prostration of recitation (the first) and one prostration of prayer (the second)
C) One prostration of recitation only
D) No prostrations of recitation in al-Hajj

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, relying on Companion statements, recognizes only one prostration of recitation in Surah al-Hajj and counts Sad as a prostration of recitation.

The Obligatory Nature of Sajdat al-Tilawah
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute on wajib status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdat al-tilawah, explain the proof from the hadith, and respond to the opposing schools' evidence.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-tilawah is wajib upon every reciter and listener—the word 'ala imposes a binding obligation.

This lesson tackles a well-known inter-madhhab dispute: is the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah) obligatory or merely recommended? The Hanafi school, relying on a clear hadith, holds it to be wajib. We will examine the proof, the objections from other schools, and the Hanafi response, so you can confidently apply and defend this ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the ruling (hukm level) and its scope: who must perform the prostration and under what conditions.
Hanafis: wajib on both reciter and listener, regardless of intent.
2
Locate the Hanafi Dalil
Find the primary evidence quoted in the text: the hadith 'al-sajdah 'ala man sami'aha wa 'ala man talaha'.
The word 'ala is key—it indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Identify the Opposing Position and Its Proof
Recognize that Malik, Shafi'i, and Hanbalis consider it sunnah, citing the incident of Zaid bin Thabit who recited Surah an-Najm without prostrating.
Understand their reasoning: if it were wajib, the Prophet would have prostrated.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
See how Hanafis counter: immediate prostration is not required; delay is permissible. The incident does not prove non-obligation.
The Prophet may have prostrated later, so the hadith does not negate obligation.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
Note the difference in practice: Hanafis must perform it and cannot omit without sin; other schools may treat it as optional.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf—the practical impact of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text

باب في سجدة التلاوة
سجدها داؤد توبسة ونحن نسجدها شكرا یعنی آنحضرت نے اپنے خطبہ میں سورہ ص کی تلاوت فرمائی (آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کے وقت ) لوگوں نے سجدہ کرنے کی تیاری کی تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ تم لوگ سجدہ کے لئے کیوں تیار ہو گئے یہ تو نبی کی تو بہ ہے اور حضور کا قول ہے کہ اس جگہ حضرت داؤد علیہ السلام نے سجدہ کیا ہے تو بہ کے طور پر اور ہم سجدہ کرتے ہیں شکر کے طور پر ہماری طرف سے اس حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ سجدہ شکر سجدہ تلاوت کے منافی نہیں ہے کیونکہ کوئی عبادت ایسی نہیں ہے جس میں شکر کے معنی نہ ہوں اور یہ بھی ثابت ہے کہ آنحضرت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے دوران خطبہ تلاوت کا سجدہ کیا ہے پس اس سے سورہ ص کے اندر آیت سجدہ کا سجدہ تلاوت ہونا ثابت ہو گیا ہے اور اگر یہ بات مان لی جائے کہ آپ نے اس موقع پر سجدہ نہیں کیا ہے تو یہ جواز تاخیر کی تعلیم کے لئے تھانہ اس لئے کہ اس جگہ سجدہ تلاوت واجب نہیں ہے۔ ہمارے مذہب کی تائید اس سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ ایک صحابی نے کہا کہ اللہ کے رسول اس بارے میں آپ کی کیا رائے ہے کہ سویا ہوا آدمی خواب میں دیکھتا ہے کہ میں سورہ ص لکھ رہا ہوں پس جب موضع سجدہ پر پہنچا تو دوات اور قلم نے سجدہ کیا۔ یہ سن کر حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ دوات اور قلم کی بہ نسبت ہم زیادہ حقدار ہیں کہ سجدہ کریں پس آپ نے حکم دیا حتی کہ آیت سجدہ پڑھی گئی اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے صحابہ کے ساتھ سجدہ کیا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ تم سجدہ میں آیت سجدہ لایسامون پر ہے جیسا کہ حضرت عمر کا قول ہے اور اسی پر عمل کرنے میں احتیاط ہے۔
ان تمام مواضع میں قاری اور سامع پر سجدہ تلاوت ہے
والسجدة واجبة في هذه المواضع على التالى والسامع سواء قصد سماع القرآن اولم يقصد لقوله عليه السلام السجدة على من سمعها وعلى من تلاها و هى كلمة ايجاب و هو غير مقيد بالقصد ترجمہ اور سجدہ کرنا ان مواضع میں واجب ہے تلاوت کرنے والے پر بھی اور سنے والے پر بھی خواہ قرآن سنے کا ارادہ کیا ہو یا ارادہ نہ کیا ہو کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ سجدہ اس پر بھی ہے جس نے سنا اور اس پر بھی ہے جس نے اس کو پڑھا۔ اور یہ کلمہ ایجاب کا ہے اور وہ قصد کے ساتھ مقید نہیں ہے۔ تشریح امام ابوالحسن قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ مذکورہ چودہ مقامات پر سجدہ کرنا قاری اور سامع دونوں پر واجب ہے سامع نے سنے کا قصد کیا ہو یا قصد نہ کیا ہو۔ امام مالک امام شافعی اور حنابلہ کے نزدیک سجدہ تلاوت سنت ہے۔ ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ زید بن ثابت نے نبی اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے سامنے سورۃ النجم کی تلاوت کی لیکن نہ زید بن ثابت نے سجدہ کیا اور نہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ۔اس واقعہ سے ثابت ہو گیا کہ سجدہ تلاوت واجب نہیں ہے بلکہ سنت ہے کیونکہ اگر واجب ہوتا تو نہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم ترک فرماتے اور نہ زید بن ثابت۔ ہماری دلیل یہ حدیث ہے السجدة على من سمعها وعلى من تلاها وجه استدلال یہ ہے کہ حدیث کے اندر لفظ علی آیا ہے جو الزام پر دلالت کرتا ہے اور یہ حدیث چونکہ قصد کی قید کے ساتھ مقید نہیں ہے اس لئے ہر سننے والے پر سجدہ تلاوت واجب ہوگا خواہ سننے کا قصد کیا ہو یا قصد نہ کیا ہو امام مالک وغیرہ کی طرف سے پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فوری طور پر سجدہ نہیں کیا اور فوری طور پر سجدہ نہ کرنا ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ نیز فوری طور پر سجدہ کرنے سے علی الاطلاق سجدہ نہ کرنا لازم نہیں آتا۔ پس ہو سکتا ہے کہ
Chapter on the prostration of recitation. David prostrated in repentance, and we prostrate in gratitude. That is, the Prophet recited Surah Sad in his sermon. When he reached the verse of prostration, the people prepared to prostrate, but he said: 'Why are you preparing to prostrate? This is the prostration of a prophet in repentance.' And the Prophet's saying: 'In this place, Prophet David prostrated in repentance, and we prostrate in gratitude from our side.' The response to this hadith is that the prostration of gratitude does not contradict the prostration of recitation, because there is no act of worship that does not contain the meaning of gratitude. And it is also established that the Prophet prostrated during his sermon for recitation. Hence, it is established that in Surah Sad, the verse of prostration requires a prostration of recitation. And if we accept that he did not prostrate on that occasion, it was to teach the permissibility of delay, not because the prostration of recitation is not obligatory there. Our school is also supported by the narration that a companion said: 'O Messenger of Allah, what is your opinion about a sleeping person who sees in a dream that he is writing Surah Sad, and when he reaches the place of prostration, the inkwell and pen prostrated?' Upon hearing this, the Prophet said: 'We are more entitled to prostrate than the inkwell and pen.' Then he ordered that the verse of prostration be recited, and he prostrated with the companions. The author of Hidayah says: 'The prostration verse in Surah Sad is upon [word unclear], as is the saying of Umar, and acting upon it is precaution.' In all these places, the prostration of recitation is upon the reciter and the listener. And the prostration is obligatory in these places upon the reciter and the listener, whether he intended to hear the Quran or not, because the Prophet said: 'The prostration is upon the one who hears it and upon the one who recites it.' This is a word of obligation, and it is not restricted by intention. Translation: The prostration in these places is obligatory upon the reciter and the listener, whether he intended to hear the Quran or not. Because the Prophet said: 'The prostration is upon the one who hears it and upon the one who recites it.' This is a word of obligation, and it is not restricted by intention. Explanation: Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said that prostration is obligatory upon both the reciter and the listener at the fourteen mentioned places, whether the listener intended to hear or not. According to Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and the Hanbalis, the prostration of recitation is sunnah. Their evidence is that Zaid bin Thabit recited Surah an-Najm in the presence of the Prophet, but neither Zaid nor the Prophet prostrated. This proves that the prostration of recitation is not obligatory but sunnah, because if it were obligatory, the Prophet would not have left it, nor would Zaid. Our evidence is the hadith: 'The prostration is upon the one who hears it and upon the one who recites it.' The point of deduction is that the word 'upon' (على) indicates obligation, and this hadith is not restricted by intention, so the prostration of recitation is obligatory upon every listener, whether or not he intended to hear. The response to the hadith presented by Imam Malik and others is that the Prophet did not prostrate immediately, and not prostrating immediately is permissible in our view. Furthermore, not prostrating immediately does not necessitate never prostrating. So it is possible that
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). The author first addresses an objection based on a hadith where the Prophet explained that the prostration in Surah Sad was one of repentance for Prophet David, not a mandatory recitation prostration. The Hanafi response is that the prostration of gratitude (shukr) does not negate the obligation of tilawah prostration, as all acts of worship contain gratitude. Moreover, the Prophet did prostrate during a sermon for recitation, establishing that the sajdah in Surah Sad is indeed a tilawah prostration. The delay was to teach permissibility of delay, not to deny obligation. A further support is the dream narration where the Prophet prostrated after hearing about the inkwell and pen. Then the author states the central ruling: sajdat al-tilawah is wajib upon the reciter and listener, whether or not the listener intended to hear, based on the Prophet's hadith 'al-sajdah 'ala man sami'aha wa 'ala man talaha' (the prostration is upon the one who hears it and upon the one who recites it). The word 'ala indicates obligation, and the hadith is unqualified by intention. Imam al-Quduri confirms that the fourteen places (of sajdah) are obligatory for both. Then the inter-madhhab dispute is presented: Imam Malik, Shafi'i, and Hanbali consider it sunnah, arguing from the incident of Zaid bin Thabit where neither he nor the Prophet prostrated. The Hanafi response is that immediate prostration is not obligatory; delay is permissible, and the Prophet may have prostrated later. Thus, the incident does not negate obligation.

Key Terms
سجدہ تلاوت (sajdat al-tilāwah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran containing a sajdah.
واجب (wājib): A religious duty established by a zanni (probable) evidence; omission without excuse is blameworthy but not as severe as fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of sajdat al-tilāwah on a person who hears a sajdah verse without intending to?
A) It is sunnah, not obligatory.
B) It is obligatory (wājib).
C) It is recommended only if the listener intended to hear.
D) It is invalid because the listener did not intend.

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-tilawah is wajib upon every reciter and hearer of a sajdah verse; the imperative 'ala in the hadith establishes obligation, and the opposing evidence does not negate it.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Sajdat al-Tilāwah for Imam and Ma'mum: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sajdah when ma'mum recites

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions regarding sajdat al-tilawah when a ma'mum recites a sajda verse and evaluate the evidence for the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
The ma'mum's recitation is legally inoperative; thus no sajdah is due from his recitation.

In congregational prayer, when the imam recites a sajdah verse, the rule is clear: both imam and ma'mum prostrate. But what happens when the ma'mum recites a sajdah verse? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn) on one side and Imam Muhammad on the other. Understanding their reasoning sharpens your ability to apply usul principles to derive rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The issue is whether the ma'mum's recitation of a sajdah verse in congregational prayer obligates any prostration (sajdat al-tilawah). Identify the two scenarios: during prayer and after prayer.
The dispute only arises when the ma'mum recites; imam reciting is unanimous.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: no prostration at all (neither in prayer nor after). Muhammad: prostration after prayer. Note which position is relied upon.
The text indicates the Shaykhayn's view is the madhhab of the majority.
3
Understand the Shaykhayn's evidence
The ma'mum is mahjur (restricted) from recitation because the imam's authority prevails. A restricted person's action has no legal effect. Analogy: a menstruating woman's recitation does not obligate sajdah because she lacks capacity for prayer.
Contrast with a junub: he retains capacity after purification, so his recitation obligates sajdah.
4
Understand Imam Muhammad's evidence
The cause (recitation and hearing) is present, and the preventer (being in prayer) is removed after prayer. Therefore, the obligation follows. He argues that performing sajdah during prayer would disrupt the proper order of imamate.
The Shaykhayn respond that the recitation was done in a state of restriction, so it does not create an obligation even after prayer.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The Shaykhayn's view is the mufta bihi. Practical consequence: if a ma'mum recites a sajdah verse, no sajdah is required from anyone. This is the operative ruling in the Hanafi school.
This ruling is based on the principle that the ma'mum's recitation is legally inoperative.

Al-Hidayah with Urdu commentary, volume 2, page 265, chapter on prostration of recitation. When the imam recites a verse of prostration, he prostrates, and the follower prostrates with him due to his obligation to follow him. And when the follower recites, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the imam and the follower do not prostrate, neither in prayer nor after finishing. Muhammad said: They prostrate when they finish, because the cause (the recitation and hearing) has been established and there is no preventer, unlike the state of prayer, because it leads to contravening the status of imamate or recitation. Their (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's) argument is that the follower is restricted from recitation because the imam's authority prevails over him, and the action of a restricted person has no legal effect, unlike the junub and menstruating woman: both are prohibited from recitation, except that prostration is not obligatory upon the menstruating woman due to her recitation, just as it is not obligatory due to her hearing, because she lacks the capacity for prayer, unlike the junub. Summary: When the imam recites a verse of prostration, the imam prostrates immediately, and the follower prostrates with him, because by intending to follow, the follower made following the imam obligatory upon himself. If he does not prostrate with the imam, it leads to opposing the imam. When the follower recites a verse of prostration, according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), neither the imam nor the follower prostrates, neither in prayer nor after finishing. This is the school of the majority of scholars. Imam Muhammad's evidence is that the cause of prostration (the follower reciting the verse and others hearing it) has been established, and the preventer (being in prayer) has been removed after prayer. The rule is that when a cause is established and the preventer is removed, the thing necessarily follows. Therefore, after finishing prayer, both imam and follower must prostrate. Unlike the state of prayer, because performing prostration in prayer would lead to contravening the status of imamate or the status of recitation. This is because if the follower (who recited) prostrates first and the imam follows him, then the imam becomes a follower and the follower becomes an imam, which contradicts the status of imamate. If the imam prostrates first and the follower follows, then the follower's recitation is not acted upon, and also the imam is not obliged to follow the follower.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage deals with the rulings of sajdat al-tilawah in congregational prayer (jama'ah). It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (ash-Shaykhayn) on one hand, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on the other. The established rule (mujma' 'alayh) is that when the imam recites a sajdah verse, he prostrates immediately, and the ma'mum must prostrate with him due to the obligation of following the imam (mutaba'ah). The dispute arises when the ma'mum recites a sajdah verse (either aloud or silently) during the prayer. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, neither the imam nor the ma'mum prostrates, neither during the prayer nor after completion. Their reasoning is that the ma'mum is restrained (mahjur) from recitation because the imam's control (tasarruf) over him is effective; thus the ma'mum's recitation is legally insignificant, like the act of a legally restricted person (mahjur). They draw an analogy to the case of a menstruating woman (ha'id) who is prohibited from recitation; even if she recites, sajdat al-tilawah is not obligatory upon her because she lacks the capacity for prayer (ahliyyat as-salah). However, they distinguish a junub (in state of major impurity) from a ha'id: a junub is also prohibited from recitation, but if he recites, sajdat al-tilawah is obligatory upon him because he retains capacity for prayer after purification. Imam Muhammad argues that after the prayer ends, the cause (the ma'mum's recitation and others hearing) is fully established, and the preventer (being in prayer) is removed. Therefore, both imam and ma'mum should prostrate after the prayer. He argues that performing the prostration during prayer would disrupt the proper order of imamate and followership: if the ma'mum prostrates first, the imam would be following him, reversing roles; if the imam prostrates first, the ma'mum's recitation is not acted upon properly.

Key Terms
مقتدی (muqtadī): The follower in congregational prayer who prays behind an imam.
متابعت (mutāba'ah): The obligation of the follower to follow the imam in all actions of the prayer, including prostrations.
محجور (mahjūr): Legally restricted person, here referring to the ma'mum who is barred from recitation due to the imam's authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what is the ruling when a ma'mum recites a sajdah verse during congregational prayer?
A) Both imam and ma'mum prostrate immediately in prayer.
B) The ma'mum prostrates alone after prayer.
C) Neither prostrates, in prayer or after.
D) Only the imam prostrates after prayer.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a ma'mum's recitation of a sajdah verse does not obligate any prostration due to his restricted legal capacity.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Sajdat al-Tilawah When the Follower Recites: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on sajdat al-tilawah when follower recites in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf vs. Imam Muhammad) on sajdat al-tilawah when the follower recites, and apply the distinction between mamnu' (prohibited) and majbur (compelled) to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
The follower's recitation is legally ineffective because he is compelled (majbur), not merely prohibited (mamnu).

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement: when a follower (mamoom) recites an ayat of sajda behind the imam, does this trigger the obligation of sajdat al-tilawah? The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say no, while Imam Muhammad says yes — after the prayer. At the heart of the dispute is a crucial distinction between two types of prohibition: one that is merely a sin (mamnu) and one that strips the act of all legal effect (majbur). Understanding this distinction will sharpen your ability to evaluate conflicting proofs within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two Hanafi positions
Identify the exact scenario: the follower recites an ayat of sajda while praying behind an imam. State the ruling according to the Shaykhayn (no prostration ever) and according to Imam Muhammad (prostration after prayer).
The Shaykhayn's view is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
2
Analyze the proof of Imam Muhammad
Muhammad argues that the cause (recitation) exists and the obstacle (being in prayer) ceases after prayer, so prostration becomes wajib. Understand his reasoning from 'the cause has been established and the obstacle is removed'.
He also cites the hadith that the talī (reciter) should lead the sajda.
3
Analyze the proof of the Shaykhayn
The Shaykhayn argue that the follower is majbur (compelled) against reciting because the imam's recitation suffices. A majbur's action has no legal effect — thus no cause, no sajda. Contrast this with a junub or ha'id who are merely mamnu (prohibited) but their recitation is effective.
They also note practical difficulties: if they were to prostrate, who leads? The talī (follower) or the imam? Either leads to violating either imamate or tilawah order.
4
Examine the qiyas (analogy) and its rebuttal
The opponent's qiyas: the follower is like a junub/ha'id because all are prohibited from reciting. In the case of junub/ha'id, listening to their recitation obligates sajda on the listener. Similarly, the imam should be obligated when the follower recites. The Shaykhayn rebut: the follower is not merely prohibited (mamnu) but legally ineffective (majbur). The junub/ha'id's recitation is effective even though sinful; the follower's recitation has zero legal weight.
This refines the illa (effective cause) from 'prohibition' to 'type of prohibition'.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) and tarjih
In practice: if a follower recites an ayat of sajda in prayer, according to the Shaykhayn no one prostrates; according to Muhammad, all prostrate after prayer. The relied-upon view is the Shaykhayn's, as given in the text.
The tarjih authority is the author of Al-Hidayah who prefers the Shaykhayn.

Chapter on the Prostration of Recitation

... [full translation omitted for brevity] ...
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the ruling of sajdat al-tilawah when the imam or the follower recites an ayat of sajda during congregational prayer. The author first states the basic rule: if the imam recites, both the imam and the follower prostrate immediately; if the follower recites, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn), neither prostrates during the prayer nor after it. Imam Muhammad holds that they should prostrate after the prayer because the cause (recitation) has occurred and the obstacle (being in prayer) has ceased. The passage then gives the reasoning: the follower is prohibited from reciting behind the imam (mamnu' an al-qira'ah), so his recitation has no legal effect; thus, no prostration is due from him or the listener (the imam). It contrasts this with the case of a junub (person in major impurity) or a menstruating woman (ha'id), who are also prohibited from reciting, but their recitation does create an obligation for the listener because they are not compelled (majbur) but merely prohibited (mamnu'). The difference is that a majbur's action is legally ineffective, while a mamnu's action is effective. Hence, the follower's recitation does not necessitate prostration for anyone.

Key Terms
ممنوع عن القراءة (mamnu' an al-qira'ah): A person who is forbidden (shar'an) from reciting the Quran, such as a junub or menstruating woman.
مجبور عن القراءة (majbur an al-qira'ah): A person who is legally prevented (by law) from reciting, such as a follower behind an imam, for whom recitation is not allowed and his recitation has no legal effect.
تالي (tālī): The person who recites the ayat of sajda (the reciter).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key reason used by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf to argue that no sajdat al-tilawah is due when a follower recites an ayat of sajda in prayer?
A) The follower is not obliged to recite, so his recitation is invalid.
B) The follower's recitation is null because he is majbur (compelled), unlike a junub who is mamnu' (prohibited).
C) The imam's recitation abrogates the follower's obligation to prostrate.
D) The sajda would invalidate the prayer if performed.

Key Takeaway
The follower's recitation behind the imam is legally ineffective (majbur), so it does not trigger sajdat al-tilawah according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Ruling on Sajdah al-Tilawah for Imam and Muqtadi in Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sajdah obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-tilawah for the imam and muqtadi during prayer and explain the distinction between mamnū‘ and majbūr.

Core Idea
Neither imam nor muqtadi performs sajdah al-tilawah in prayer because the muqtadi's recitation is legally ineffective.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-tilawah during congregational prayer. The text from Al-Hidayah presents the position of the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and refutes a potential analogy with the junub and menstruating woman. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the rules of prostration in the correct context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Determine whether the imam and muqtadi are required to perform sajdah al-tilawah when a prostration verse is recited during congregational prayer.
The disagreement is within the Hanafi school itself, not between madhhabs.
2
State the Hanafi position (Shaykhayn)
The relied-upon view is that neither the imam nor the muqtadi prostrates during prayer. The muqtadi is prohibited from recitation behind the imam, so his recitation has no legal effect.
The hadith 'Whoever has an imam, the imam's recitation is his recitation' is the primary evidence.
3
Understand the qiyas refuted
An analogy is drawn: just as a junub or menstruating woman's recitation obligates prostration on the hearer, so should the muqtadi's recitation obligate the imam. The text refutes this by distinguishing mamnū‘ from majbūr.
The qiyas is based on the similarity of prohibition.
4
Learn the mamnū‘/majbūr distinction
Mamnū‘ (prohibited) actions still have legal effect in certain circumstances; majbūr (compelled/incapable) actions have no effect. The junub and menstruating woman are mamnū‘, while the muqtadi is majbūr.
Example: a corrupt sale (mamnū‘) can transfer ownership, but a sale by a minor (majbūr) cannot.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, during congregational prayer, if a prostration verse is recited, neither the imam nor the followers perform sajdah al-tilawah. Performing it would be an unnecessary action that could invalidate the prayer.
This is the mufta bihi position of the Shaykhayn.

اور مجبور کے درمیان فرق یہ ہے کہ شور عنہ کا فعل غیر معتبر ہوتا ہے نہ حرام ہوتا ہے ورنہ مکروہ اور منوع ( جسکو منع کیا گیا ہے ) کا فعل معتبر ہوتا ہے خواہ حرام ہو یا مکر وہ مثلا بیع فاسد ممنوع (منہی ) ہے لیکن اگر کسی نے بیچ فاسد کر لی اور مشتری نے مبیع پر قبضہ کر لیا تو مشتری کی ملک ثابت ہو جائے گی اور اگر مجورعنہ مثل نابالغ بچہ یا مجنون نے عقد بیع کا معاملہ کیا اور مشتری نے مبیع پر قبضہ بھی کر لیا تو مشتری کے لئے ملک ثابت نہ ہوگی پس چونکہ جنبی اور حائضہ ممنوع عن القرآة ہیں نہ کہ مجور عن القرآت اس لئے ان کی تلاوت سبب سجدہ ہوگی ۔ اور اس کا یہ اثر ہوگا کہ جو شخص ان سے آیت سجدہ کی سماعت کرے گا اس پر سجدہ تلاوت واجب ہوگا۔ اس کے برخلاف مقتدی کہ وہ مجحور عن القرأۃ ہے نہ اس کی قرآت معتبر ہو گی اور نہ ہی سبب سجدہ ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ممنوع عن القراۃ ہونے میں جنبی اور حائضہ دونوں برابر ہیں لیکن اتنا فرق ہے کہ حائضہ عورت پر نہ خود اپنی تلاوت سے سجدہ واجب ہوگا اور نہ دوسرے کی تلاوت سننے سے اور جنبی آدمی آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کرے تب بھی سجدہ تلاوت واجب ہوگا اور اگر دوسرے سے سنے تب بھی واجب ہوگا ۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ سجدہ تلاوت واجب ہونے میں نماز کی اہمیت معتبر ہو گی خواہ ادا ہو خواہ قضاء ہو اور حائضہ عورت میں نماز کی اہلیت دونوں طرح نہیں ہے ۔ اور جنبی کے اندر نماز کی اہلیت موجود ہے بایں طور کہ اگر وقت کے اندراندر غسل کر لیا تو ا دا واجب ہوگی ورنہ قضاء واجب ہوگی ۔
Chapter on the prostration of recitation. And the reciter, i.e., the follower, if he follows him, then it would go against the context of recitation, because the reciter is the imam of the listener. Therefore, the reciter's prostration must come first. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said to the reciter: 'You are our imam; if you prostrate, we prostrate with you.' The conclusion is that the prostration is obligatory upon the reciter and is prior. Here the matter became reversed: the imam prostrated first and the reciter later. In any case, since performing prostration during prayer necessarily entails some defect, therefore during prayer neither the imam nor the follower should prostrate. The proof of the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that for the follower behind the imam, recitation is prohibited by law. Recitation for the follower is prohibited because the imam's action is effective upon him, meaning the imam's recitation counts as recitation on behalf of the follower. As the beloved of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever has an imam, the imam's recitation is his recitation.' In any case, the follower is prohibited from recitation, and whoever is prevented from an action has no ruling for that action. Therefore, since the follower is prohibited from recitation, his recitation has no ruling, and when his recitation has no ruling, then prostration of recitation is not obligatory upon him. And when the prostration is not obligatory upon the reciter, then it is also not obligatory upon the listener, i.e., the imam. This is a response to an analogy with the junub and the menstruating woman. The analogy is that the follower, in being prohibited from recitation, resembles the junub and menstruating woman, and prostration becomes obligatory by hearing their recitation. That is, if one of them recites a verse of prostration and another person hears it, then prostration of recitation becomes obligatory upon the hearer. Similarly, if the follower, though prohibited from recitation, actually recites a verse of prostration and the imam hears his recitation, then prostration should be obligatory upon the imam, whereas the two shaykhs do not hold obligatory prostration even for the imam. The answer: The junub and menstruating woman are prohibited from recitation (mamnū‘), while the follower is compelled/incapable (majbūr). The difference between the prohibited (mamnū‘) and the compelled (majbūr) is that the action of the one prohibited is considered invalid, not sinful or disliked, while the action of the one prohibited is considered valid, whether it is sinful or disliked. For example, a corrupt sale is prohibited, but if someone makes a corrupt sale and the buyer takes possession, the buyer's ownership is established. But if a person who is compelled, like a minor or insane person, makes a sale and the buyer takes possession, the buyer's ownership is not established. Therefore, since the junub and menstruating woman are prohibited from recitation, not compelled, their recitation is a cause for prostration. And its effect is that whoever hears the verse of prostration from them, prostration of recitation becomes obligatory. In contrast, the follower is compelled in recitation, so his recitation is not valid nor a cause for prostration. The author of the Hidayah says that the junub and menstruating woman are equal in being prohibited from recitation, but there is a difference: For the menstruating woman, prostration is not obligatory by her own recitation nor by hearing another's recitation. For the junub man, if he recites a verse of prostration, prostration is obligatory, and if he hears from another, it is also obligatory. The reason is that for the obligation of prostration of recitation, the capacity for prayer is considered, whether performed on time or as make-up. The menstruating woman lacks the capacity for prayer in both ways, while the junub has the capacity for prayer in that if he performs ghusl within the time, the prayer is obligatory as on time, otherwise as make-up.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the imam and muqtadi (follower) should perform sajdah al-tilawah during prayer when a verse of prostration is recited. The text presents the position of the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) that neither should prostrate during prayer. The reasoning: the muqtadi is prohibited from reciting behind the imam, as per the hadith that the imam's recitation suffices for the follower. Since the muqtadi's recitation has no legal effect, it cannot trigger the obligation of sajdah al-tilawah. Consequently, the imam who hears the muqtadi's recitation also does not have to prostrate. The text then addresses a potential qiyas (analogy) comparing the muqtadi to a junub (person in major impurity) or menstruating woman: if they recite a prostration verse, the hearer must prostrate. The response distinguishes between mamnū‘ (prohibited from recitation) and majbūr (compelled/incapable). The junub and menstruating woman are mamnū‘—their action is valid in terms of being a cause for others' obligation—while the muqtadi is majbūr, so his recitation has no validity at all. The author of Hidayah further notes an internal difference: a menstruating woman's recitation does not obligate prostration even for a hearer, while a junub's does, because the menstruating woman lacks the capacity for prayer entirely within that state.

Key Terms
سجدہ تلاوت (sajdah al-tilawah): Prostration of recitation, an act required upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran that contains a command to prostrate.
مقتدی (muqtadi): A person praying behind an imam, i.e., a follower in congregational prayer.
ممنوع عن القرآۃ (mamnū‘ ‘an al-qirā’ah): A person legally prohibited from reciting the Quran, such as a junub or menstruating woman, or a muqtadi behind the imam.
مجبور (majbūr): A person who is compelled or legally incapable of performing an action, such that their action has no legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Shaykhayn), why does the imam not have to perform sajdah al-tilawah when the muqtadi recites a prostration verse in prayer?
A) Because the muqtadi is prohibited from recitation, so his recitation has no legal effect.
B) Because the imam is also prohibited from hearing recitation.
C) Because sajdah al-tilawah is not required in prayer at all.
D) Because the muqtadi cannot recite a prostration verse.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-tilawah is not performed during congregational prayer because the muqtadi's recitation is legally ineffective, and the imam's recitation suffices.
