Ruling for One Outside Prayer Hearing a Prostration Verse
Ruling on sajdah for a person outside prayer hearing from imam or muqtadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-tilawah for a person outside prayer who hears a prostration verse from the imam or muqtadi, and explain the rationale using the concept of majbūr.

Core Idea
The muqtadi's compulsion does not exempt outsiders from sajdah al-tilawah.

This passage clarifies a common scenario: a person not in prayer hears a prostration verse recited by the imam or a muqtadi who is praying. Is sajdah al-tilawah still obligatory? The Hanafi school answers yes, based on a key principle about the scope of the muqtadi's special status. We will unpack the ruling, the proof, and an internal scholarly difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Sajdah al-tilawah. What is the ruling? It is wajib for a person who hears a prostration verse, even if the reciter is the imam or muqtadi in prayer and the hearer is outside prayer.
The ruling is based on general obligation of sajdah al-tilawah upon hearing.
2
Understand the scenario and the potential objection
The muqtadi is majbūr ‘an al-qirā’ah (compelled from recitation) – his recitation has no legal effect. One might think, therefore, that hearing from him is like hearing nothing, so no sajdah is required. The text rejects this.
The concept of 'majbūr' is specific to the muqtadi's own obligation, not to others.
3
Grasp the proof (dalīl aqlī)
The proof: The 'compulsion' (hajr) is established only regarding the muqtadis themselves; it does not extend beyond them. Since it does not extend, outsiders are affected normally by the recitation they hear.
This is a rational proof (dalīl aqlī) based on the limited scope of the legal impediment.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
The text mentions a disagreement: the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that an outsider who hears from the muqtadi and then joins the prayer does not need to prostrate. Imam Muhammad (in another narration) holds he does. The correct view (qawl sahīh) is that he must prostrate even after joining.
This is an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf; the muftā bihi is the qawl sahīh.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author of Hidayah designates the view that the outsider must prostrate as the correct one. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The tarjīh comes from the later Hanafi tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نماز سے باہر آیت سجدہ سننے والے پر سجدہ تلاوت لازم ہے ولو سمعها رجل خارج الصلوة سجدها هو الصحيح لان الحجر ثبت في حقهم فلا يعدوهم رجمہ اور اگر (امام یا مقتدی سے ) آیت سجدہ کو کسی ایسے آدمی نے سنا جو خارج صلوۃ ہے تو وہ سجدہ تلاوت کرے یہی قول صحیح ہے یونکہ مجبور ہونا مقتدیوں کے حق میں ثابت ہوا ہے لہذا ان سے متجاوز نہ ہو گا۔ شریح مسئلہ کسی ایسے آدمی نے جو نماز سے باہر ہے ایام یا مقتدی سے سجدہ کی آیت سنی اور شخص آیت سجدہ سن کر نماز میں شامل بھی ہیں ہوا تو بالاتفاق اس پر سجدہ تلاوت واجب ہوگا یہی قول صحیح ہے بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ یہ حکم مختلف فیہ چنانچہ پیخین کے نزدیک یہ ی سجدہ نہیں کرے گا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک سجدہ کرے گا۔ قول صحیح کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مجور عن القرآت ہونا مقتدیوں کے حق میں ثابت ہوا ہے لہذا ان سے متجاوز نہ ہوگا اور جب ان سے متجاوز نہ ہوا تو ان کے علاوہ دوسرے لوگوں پر اس کا اثر بھی نہ ہوگا اور جب مقتدیوں کے مادہ دوسروں پر مجور عن القرآت ہونے کا اثر نہیں پڑا تو آیت سجدہ سنے کی وجہ سے ان پر سجدہ واجب ہوگا۔
The prostration of recitation is obligatory upon the one who hears a prostration verse outside of prayer. And if he hears it outside prayer, he should prostrate; that is the correct statement because the restriction (hajr) is established regarding them (the muqtadis) so it does not apply to others. And if a person who is outside prayer hears a prostration verse from the imam or the muqtadi, then he should perform the prostration of recitation; this is the correct saying because the compulsion (majbūr) is established regarding the muqtadis, so it does not extend beyond them. Explanation of the issue: A person who is outside prayer heard a prostration verse from the imam or the muqtadi, and that person then also joins the prayer; then by consensus, prostration of recitation is obligatory upon him. This is the correct saying. Some scholars have said that this ruling is disputed. Thus, according to the two shaykhs, he will not prostrate, and according to Imam Muhammad, he will prostrate. The proof of the correct saying is that being compelled from recitation is established regarding the muqtadis, so it does not extend beyond them. And when it does not extend beyond them, its effect does not apply to other people. And when the effect of being compelled from recitation does not affect others, then due to hearing the prostration verse, prostration is obligatory upon them.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for a person who is not in prayer and hears a prostration verse recited by the imam or muqtadi who are in prayer. The text states that the correct view is that the outsider must perform sajdah al-tilawah. The reason is that the compulsion (majbūr) of the muqtadi is specific to the prayer context and does not extend to those outside. Therefore, the outsider's obligation remains. The text also addresses a scenario where the outsider, after hearing the verse, joins the prayer. In that case, by consensus, he must still prostrate. However, there is an internal dispute: according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he does not prostrate after joining; according to Imam Muhammad alone (the text says 'Imam Muhammad' but likely refers to the narrations from him), he does prostrate. The preferred view (qawl sahīh) is that he must prostrate, as the compulsion does not affect him.

Key Terms
مجبور عن القرآۃ (majbūr ‘an al-qirā’ah): A person who is legally compelled or incapable of recitation, such as a minor or insane person, or here the muqtadi whose recitation has no effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a person outside prayer who hears a prostration verse recited by the muqtadi in prayer, according to the correct view in the Hidayah?
A) He must perform sajdah al-tilawah.
B) He does not perform sajdah because the muqtadi's recitation has no effect.
C) He must perform sajdah only if he hears it from the imam.
D) He cannot perform sajdah outside prayer.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of sajdah al-tilawah for one outside prayer is not negated by the muqtadi's compulsion; the outsider must perform sajdah because the compulsion is limited to the prayer context.

Sajdah al-Tilawah During Prayer from a Non-Participant
Ruling on sajdah when prayed hear prostration verse from someone not in their prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing sajdah al-tilawah during prayer when the reciter is not in the same prayer, and explain the reason based on the definition of prayer actions (af‘āl al-ṣalāh).

Core Idea
Only legislated prayer actions (fard, wajib, sunnah) may be performed during prayer; hearing a prostration verse is not one of them.

What happens when you are in the middle of prayer and someone outside your congregation recites a prostration verse? According to the Hanafi school, you cannot simply prostrate during the prayer because that action is not part of the prescribed actions of prayer. This lesson examines the reasoning behind this ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes a group of people in prayer who hear a prostration verse recited by someone not participating in their prayer.
2
State the ruling
They must not perform sajdah al-tilawah during the prayer; they must perform it after completing the prayer.
The ruling is given clearly in the first sentence.
3
Understand the reason (illa)
The act of hearing is not an action (fi‘l) of prayer. The only actions permitted during prayer are those legislated as fard, wajib, or sunnah of the prayer itself.
This is the key principle: af‘āl al-ṣalāh are limited.
4
Apply the principle to the case
Since hearing a prostration verse is not among the legislated actions, performing an extra sajdah during the prayer would be an impermissible addition.
Thus, the sajdah must be postponed.
5
Confirm the obligation after prayer
The cause (sabab) of wajib sajdah al-tilawah – hearing the verse – is still present, so it becomes wajib to perform after the prayer ends.
The obligation is not nullified by the prayer; it is merely deferred.

ران سمعوا وهم فى الصلوة سجدة من رجل ليس معهم فى الصلواة لم يسجدوها في الصلوة لانها ليست متلانية لان سماعهم هذه السجدة ليس من افعال الصلوة و سجدو ها بعدها لتحقق سيها رجمہ اور اگر لوگوں نے درانحالیکہ وہ نماز میں ہیں کسی ایسے آدمی سے آیت سجدہ کو نا جو ان کے ساتھ نماز میں نہیں تو یہ لوگ نماز میں مجدہ نہ کریں کیونکہ یہ سجدہ نماز کا سجدہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ ان لوگوں کا اس آیت سجدہ کو سن لینا نماز کے افعال سے نہیں ہے اور نماز کے بعد سجدہ کریں کیونکہ اس کا سبب متحقق ہو چکا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کچھ لوگوں نے بحالت نماز کسی ایسے شخص سے آیت سجدہ سنی جو ان کے ساتھ نماز میں شریک نہیں ہے تو یہ لوگ نماز کی حالت میں سجدہ تلاوت نہ کریں کیونکہ یہ سجدہ نماز کا سجدہ نہیں ہے اور نماز کا سجدہ اس لئے نہیں ہے کہ ان لوگوں کا اس آیت سجدہ کو سننا نماز کے افعال میں سے نہیں ہے کیونکہ نماز کے افعال یا تو فرض ہوتے ہیں یا واجب یا سنت اس آیت سجدہ کو سننا ان میں ت کچھ بھی نہیں ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ سجدہ نماز کے افعال میں سے نہیں ہے اور جو چیز نماز کے افعال میں سے نہ ہو اس کا نماز کے اندر ادا کرنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ یہ لوگ نماز کے اندر سجدہ تلاوت نہ کریں۔ ہاں البتہ نماز کے بعد سجدہ تلاوت کرنا واجب ہوگا کیونکہ تبہ کا سبب یعنی آیت سجدہ کا سننا پایا گیا۔
And if they hear while they are in prayer a prostration verse from a man who is not with them in the prayer, they do not prostrate for it in the prayer because it is not a recited prostration (mutlawa?), because their hearing this prostration is not from the actions of the prayer. And they prostrate for it after the prayer because its cause has been realized. And if people, while they are in prayer, hear a prostration verse from a person who is not participating with them in the prayer, then these people should not perform the prostration of recitation in the prayer because this is not a prostration of the prayer. And it is not a prostration of the prayer because these people's hearing of this prostration verse is not from the actions of the prayer. The actions of the prayer are either obligatory (fard), or necessary (wajib), or sunnah. Hearing this prostration verse is none of these. The conclusion is that the prostration is not from the actions of the prayer, and it is not permissible to perform something that is not from the actions of the prayer during the prayer. So it is established that these people should not perform the prostration of recitation in the prayer. Yes, after the prayer, it is obligatory to perform the prostration of recitation because its cause, i.e., hearing the prostration verse, has been realized.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: a group of people are in prayer, and an outsider (someone not in their prayer) recites a prostration verse. The ruling is that they do not perform the sajdah during the prayer itself. The reason is that hearing this verse is not an action of the prayer; the actions of prayer are only what are legislated as part of the prayer (fard, wajib, sunnah). Since hearing is not one of them, performing extra prostrations within the prayer would be impermissible. However, the obligation of sajdah al-tilawah is still triggered by hearing the verse, so they must perform it after completing the prayer. The text emphasizes that this is not a prostration of the prayer itself, but a separate obligation that cannot be fulfilled during the prayer.

Key Terms
افعال الصلوة (af‘āl al-ṣalāh): The actions that constitute the prayer, such as standing, bowing, prostrating, etc., which are either fard, wajib, or sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person in prayer hears a prostration verse recited by someone who is not in the same prayer, what should he do according to the Hanafi school?
A) Perform sajdah al-tilawah immediately within the prayer.
B) Not perform sajdah at all because the reciter is not in prayer.
C) Perform sajdah al-tilawah after completing the prayer.
D) Recite the verse himself to make it part of prayer.

Key Takeaway
Hearing a prostration verse during prayer from a non-participant does not permit performing sajdah al-tilawah in the prayer; it must be done after the prayer because it is not a prayer action.

Sajdah al-Tilawah for the Hearer Outside Prayer
States ruling and proof for sajdah al-tilawah upon hearing from a praying person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-tilawah for a person outside prayer who hears a sajdah verse from a praying person, explain the proof based on the scope of jabr, and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Core Idea
The exemption (jabr) for the reciter does not extend to the hearer; hearing a sajdah verse obligates sajdah even if the reciter is in prayer.

When a person is in prayer and recites a verse of sajdah, the obligation for the hearer remains intact even though the reciter is engaged in his own prayer. This lesson clarifies the correct Hanafi position, reconciling the principles of obligation and exemption within the acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Determine the parties: a person in prayer reciting a sajdah verse, and a person outside prayer who hears that verse.
The reciter may be an imam or a follower in congregation.
2
State the Ruling
The correct Hanafi position is that the hearer must perform sajdah al-tilawah.
This is the mufta bihi view attributed to Imam Muhammad.
3
Understand the Proof (Talil)
The exemption (jabr) - meaning the reciter is not compelled to make others hear - applies only to the reciter, not the hearer. Therefore, the cause (hearing) still obligates the hearer.
Jabr is a technical term in Hanafi usul for a legal dispensation that does not transcend its subject.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the hearer does not perform sajdah. Their reasoning would be that the exemption somehow extends, but the text clarifies it does not.
The tarjih (preference) is with Imam Muhammad's view, stated as 'huwa al-sahih'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سمعها رجل خارج الصلوة سجدها هو الصحيح لان الحجر ثبت في حقهم فلا يعدوهم
And if a man outside prayer hears it [a verse of sajdah], he performs sajdah; this is the correct [view] because the compulsion (jabr) is established with respect to them [the reciters], so it does not transcend them.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding sajdah al-tilawah for a person who is not in prayer but hears a verse of prostration from someone who is praying (imam or follower). The correct position according to the Hanafi school is that such a person must perform the sajdah. The proof given is that the exemption (jabr) - meaning the ruling that exempts the reciter from being forced to make others hear - applies only to the reciters (the praying persons), not to the hearer. Therefore, the obligation of sajdah upon hearing remains on the outsider. The text notes that some scholars (specifically Shaykhayn: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) disagree and hold that the outsider does not perform sajdah, while Imam Muhammad says he does. The correct opinion (al-sahih) is that sajdah is wajib. This is because the legal cause (sabab) for sajdah is hearing the verse, and the exemption for the reciter does not negate that cause for the hearer.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran that commands prostration.
الجبر (al-jabr): The legal exemption or compulsion that applies specifically to the reciter, not to the hearer, in the context of sajdah obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi position, what must a person who is outside prayer do upon hearing a sajdah verse from someone who is in prayer?
A) He must perform sajdah immediately within the same prayer.
B) He must perform sajdah after the praying person completes their prayer.
C) He must perform sajdah on his own, regardless of the reciter's prayer status.
D) He is not required to perform sajdah at all.

Key Takeaway
The person outside prayer must perform sajdah al-tilawah upon hearing a sajdah verse from a praying person because the exemption (jabr) is specific to the reciter.

Sajdah from an Outsider’s Recitation During Prayer
Ruling that sajdah al-tilawah from external recitation during prayer is postponed until after prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that sajdah al-tilawah resulting from hearing a verse recited by someone not in your prayer must be postponed until after the prayer.

Core Idea
Hearing a sajdah verse from an outsider does not become part of your prayer — perform sajdah after.

Imagine you are in the middle of your salah and hear someone nearby recite a verse of sajdah. Your instinct might be to prostrate immediately. However, the Hanafi school teaches that such an action is not part of the prayer itself and must be delayed. This lesson examines the precise reasoning behind this ruling and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the passage and note the specific condition: the reciter is not part of the prayer. The ruling is that sajdah is not performed during the prayer.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The passage provides a talil (reasoning): hearing the sajdah is not from the actions of prayer (afʿāl al-ṣalāh). Therefore, performing it would be an extraneous action.
No explicit Quran or Hadith cited; the proof is the definition of what constitutes the prayer.
3
Trace the legal implication
Since the sajdah is not part of the prayer’s actions, performing it during the prayer would be an addition not permitted. The cause (sabab) of the sajdah—hearing the verse—is fulfilled, so it becomes obligatory, but its place is after the prayer.
4
Confirm the practical outcome (thamarah)
The practical result: one must complete the current prayer and then perform the sajdah al-tilawah. If one were to perform it during prayer, the prayer might become invalid due to adding an extra action.
5
Note the absence of ikhtilaf
The passage indicates that this ruling is agreed upon within the Hanafi school (no intra-madhhab dispute) and is the standard position (zahir al-riwayah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سمعوا وهم فى الصلاة سجدة من رجل ليس معهم فى الصلاة لم يسجدوها في الصلاة لأنها ليست متلانية لأن سماعهم هذه السجدة ليس من أفعال الصلاة وسجدوها بعدها لتحقق سببها
And if they hear while in prayer a sajdah [verse] from a man who is not with them in prayer, they do not perform sajdah during the prayer because it is not related to them, because their hearing this sajdah is not from the actions of prayer, and they perform it after it [the prayer] due to the verification of its cause.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the scenario where a group of people in prayer hear a sajdah verse from someone who is not participating in their prayer. The ruling is that they should not perform sajdah al-tilawah during the prayer itself, because the act of hearing the verse is not part of the actions of prayer (af'al al-salah). In Hanafi fiqh, inserting an action that is not from the prayer invalidates it if it is a significant addition, but here they are instructed to postpone the sajdah until after the prayer. The reason is that the cause (sabab) for the sajdah — hearing the verse — has occurred, so it becomes obligatory, but it cannot be performed during the prayer because it is not an act of prayer. Therefore, they must perform it after completing their salah.

Key Terms
أفعال الصلاة (afʿāl al-ṣalāh): The specific actions that constitute the prayer, such as qiyam, ruku, sujud, recitation, etc. Hearing a verse from an outsider is not among them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should a group of praying individuals perform sajdah al-tilawah after hearing a sajdah verse from someone not in their prayer?
A) Immediately during the prayer.
B) After completing the prayer.
C) Only if the reciter is the imam.
D) They need not perform it at all.

Key Takeaway
Hearing a sajdah verse from an outsider does not make the sajdah part of the prayer; it must be performed after completing salah.

Salah — Prayer

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Sajdah During Prayer: Does It Invalidate the Prayer?
Ruling on sajdah during prayer with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing sajdah al-tilawah during prayer, distinguish the positions of Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Sajdah during prayer is deficient, but the prayer remains valid according to the majority.

In the previous lesson, we learned that performing sajdah al-tilawah during prayer is prohibited. But what if someone inadvertently does it? Does that invalidate the entire prayer or is it just a deficient sajdah that must be repeated? This passage from al-Hidayah addresses two questions: first, the ruling on the sajdah itself, and second, the effect on the prayer. The answer reveals an important intra-Hanafi dispute between Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its deficiency
The passage rules that if someone performs sajdah al-tilawah during prayer, the sajdah is invalid and does not suffice. The reason given is that it is 'deficient due to the prohibition' (nāqiṣ li-makān al-nahy). Understand that the prohibition taints the act, so it does not fulfill the wajib.
The deficiency does not arise from the sajdah's form but from its context.
2
Understand the requirement to repeat the sajdah
The text says: 'They repeat it because its cause has arisen.' The cause (sabab) is hearing a sajdah verse; it is confirmed regardless of the prohibition. Therefore, the sajdah must be performed again after the prayer to fulfill the obligation.
The sajdah is not waived, just postponed.
3
Analyse the dispute on prayer validity
The passage states that according to Shaykhayn, the prayer is not repeated (i.e., remains valid) because 'mere sajdah does not contradict the ihram of prayer.' Then it cites a contrary transmission from al-Nawadir that the prayer becomes invalid 'because they added to it what is not from it.' This is attributed to Imam Muhammad. Trace the logical basis: Shaykhayn focus on the nature of the added act (it does not break ihram), while Imam Muhammad focuses on the addition of a non-prayer act.
This is a classic example of usuli difference: the definition of mufsidat.
4
Compare the proofs (talīl)
Shaykhayn's proof: Adding an act that does not contradict the essence (mahiyyah) of prayer does not invalidate. The ihram of prayer is only broken by acts that are incompatible with it (like talking, eating). A sajdah, though prohibited, is still a form of worship and does not negate the state of prayer. Imam Muhammad's proof: Any voluntary addition of an action not originally part of the prayer is a major addition (ziyādah) that invalidates, based on the principle that the prayer is a sequence of prescribed movements; adding extra is like interrupting it.
The dispute hinges on whether 'adding something not from it' necessarily invalidates.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author (al-Marghinani) clearly states 'they do not repeat the prayer' without qualification, indicating that the view of Shaykhayn is the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah). The Nawadir transmission is mentioned but not adopted. In fatwa, the prayer remains valid and only the sajdah must be repeated.
This is the operative ruling for practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سجدوها فى الصلاة لم يجزهم لأنه ناقص لمكان النهى فلا يتادى به الكامل. قال واعادوها لتفرد سببها ولم يعيدوا الصلاة لأن مجرد السجدة لا ينافي إحرام الصلاة وفي النوادر أنها تفسد لأنهم زادوا فيها ما ليس منها وقيل هو قول محمد
And if they perform it [sajdah] during the prayer, it does not suffice them because it is deficient due to the prohibition, so the complete [obligation] is not fulfilled by it. He said: And they repeat it because its cause has arisen, and they do not repeat the prayer because mere sajdah does not contradict the inviolability of prayer. In the Nawadir, it invalidates [the prayer] because they added to it what is not from it. And it is said this is the saying of Muhammad.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage deals with two rulings: first, if the praying individuals erroneously perform sajdah al-tilawah during the prayer (which is prohibited as per the previous lesson), that sajdah is invalid and does not fulfill the obligation. The reason given is that the sajdah is deficient because it was performed in a prohibited context (during prayer when prohibited), so the complete wajib is not fulfilled. Second, the author (al-Marghinani) states that they must repeat the sajdah after the prayer because its cause (hearing) is confirmed, but they do not need to repeat the prayer itself because merely performing a prohibited sajdah does not nullify the prayer (it does not contradict the ihram of prayer). However, the text notes a transmission from the Nawadir (rare narrations) that the prayer becomes invalid because they added something not part of the prayer to it. This is attributed to Imam Muhammad. Thus, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the prayer remains valid, while Imam Muhammad holds it becomes invalid because adding a non-prayer act is a major addition that invalidates. The relied-upon position (for fatwa) is the view of Shaykhayn, as stated in the text.

Key Terms
إحرام الصلاة (iḥrām al-ṣalāh): The state of consecration or inviolability that begins with takbirat al-ihram; performing a prohibited action does not necessarily contradict it.
السجدة (al-sajdah): The prostration of recitation (sajdah al-tilawah), which may be performed in or outside prayer.
النوادر (al-nawādir): The rare transmissions (as opposed to Zahir al-Riwayah), often containing positions of individual imams like Imam Muhammad that may not be the relied-upon view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the effect on the prayer if one performs sajdah al-tilawah during the prayer after hearing a sajdah verse from someone not in the prayer?
A) The prayer is invalidated, and both sajdah and prayer must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid, and the sajdah is valid as well.
C) The prayer is valid, but the sajdah must be repeated after the prayer.
D) The sajdah is valid, but the prayer becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
Performing sajdah al-tilawah during prayer results in a deficient sajdah that must be repeated, but the prayer itself remains valid according to the majority Hanafi view.

Sajdah Tilawah in Prayer: Deficient Performance
Ruling that sajdah tilawah in prayer is deficient

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why a sajdah tilawah performed in prayer (for a verse heard outside) does not fulfill the wajib and identify the underlying principle.

Core Idea
A deficient act cannot fulfill a complete wajib obligation.

In the Hanafi school, reciting or hearing an ayah of sajdah makes sajdah tilawah wajib. But what if, instead of prostrating immediately outside prayer, you delay it and then prostrate during the next prayer? The ruling might surprise you: the sajdah in prayer does not count. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this seemingly strict rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing sajdah tilawah inside the prayer for an external recitation. The ruling is that it does not fulfill the wajib obligation.
2
Understand the reason: deficiency
The sajdah is deficient because it is done in a prohibited context—inserting a foreign act (sajdah tilawah) into prayer, which is not part of the prayer's actions.
Prohibition here means the act is not allowed in prayer, not that the prayer becomes invalid.
3
Apply the principle
The principle is: a complete wajib cannot be fulfilled by a deficient performance. Since the sajdah experienced deficiency, it cannot substitute for the complete wajib.
This principle is a foundational qa'ida in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Note the consequence for prayer
The prayer itself remains valid because the prostration does not contradict the essence of prayer; only the sajdah tilawah obligation remains unfulfilled.
The act of prostration in prayer is not harmful to prayer, but it is not sufficient for the external wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سجدوها فى الصلوة لم يجزهم لانه ناقص لمكان النهى فلا يتادى به الكامل ترجمہ اور اگر ان لوگوں نے نماز کے اندر ہی سجدہ کر لیا تو ان کو کافی نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہ ادا ناقص ہے اس لئے کہ نبی [؟] موجود ہے۔ پس اس سے کامل ادانہ ہو گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ پہلے مسئلہ میں گذر چکا ہے کہ ان لوگوں کے لئے نماز کے اندر سجدہ کرنا ممنوع ہے لیکن اس ممانعت کے باوجود اگر بدہ [؟] کر لیا تو وہ معتبر نہ ہوگا البتہ نماز بھی فاسد نہ ہوگی۔ سجدہ معتبر نہ ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ سجدہ ناقص ہے اس لئے کہ شریعت نے نماز کے اندر ہر اس چیز کو داخل کرنے سے منع کیا ہے جو چیز نماز کے افعال سے نہ ہو۔ بہر حال یہ سجدہ ناقص ہے اور سماع کی وجہ سے جو سجدہ واجب ہوا ہے وہ کامل ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ واجب کامل ناقص طور پر ادا کرنے سے ادا نہیں ہوتا اس لئے ان حضرات کے نماز کے اندر سجدہ کرنے سے سجدہ تلاوت ادا نہ ہوگا۔
And if they perform sajdah [for it] in prayer, it will not suffice for them because it is deficient due to the prohibition, so the complete [obligation] is not fulfilled by it. Translation: And if these people performed sajdah within prayer, it will not be sufficient for them because this performance is deficient due to the presence of prohibition. So the complete performance will not be achieved by it. Explanation: The issue has passed in the previous issue that for these people, performing sajdah in prayer is prohibited. But despite this prohibition, if they did it, it is not valid; however, the prayer is not invalidated. The proof that the sajdah is not valid is that this sajdah is deficient because the Shariah has prohibited inserting into prayer anything that is not from the actions of prayer. In any case, this sajdah is deficient, and the sajdah made obligatory by hearing is complete, and the rule is that a complete obligation is not fulfilled by performing it deficiently. Therefore, by their performing sajdah in prayer, the sajdah of recitation is not fulfilled.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that if a person hears a verse of sajdah outside prayer, but then performs the sajdah during prayer (for example, by joining the imam's sajdah or intentionally prostrating), that sajdah does not fulfill the obligation of sajdah tilawah. The reason is that such a sajdah is deficient because the Shariah prohibits inserting into prayer any act not part of its prescribed actions. Since the sajdah tilawah became obligatory due to hearing, it is a complete obligation, and a deficient act cannot substitute for a complete one. The passage also clarifies that while the sajdah itself is not valid, the prayer remains valid because the act of prostration does not contradict the essence of prayer. The underlying principle (qa'ida) is that an incomplete performance cannot fulfill a complete wajib.

Key Terms
سجدۃ التلاوة (sajdah al-tilawah): The prostration required upon reciting or hearing a verse of prostration in the Quran.
ناقص (naaqis): Deficient; an act performed in a prohibited context, lacking the required completeness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hears an ayah of sajdah outside prayer and then performs a prostration during the prayer, what is the ruling?
A) The sajdah is valid and the obligation is fulfilled.
B) The sajdah is not valid and must be repeated outside prayer; the prayer is also invalid.
C) The sajdah is not valid and must be repeated outside prayer, but the prayer remains valid.
D) The sajdah is valid only if the person intended it for the recitation.

Key Takeaway
A complete wajib obligation cannot be fulfilled by a deficient act; sajdah tilawah performed in prayer for an external recitation is deficient and thus invalid.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Extra Sajdah Invalidating Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on extra sajdah invalidity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether an invalid sajdah during prayer invalidates the prayer, and explain the basis of the intra-Hanafi dispute between the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
Adding less than a rak'ah does not invalidate prayer, per the two shaykhs; but Imam Muhammad holds any extraneous addition invalidates.

In this passage from Ashraf ul Hadaya, the author clarifies a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute regarding an invalid sajdah performed during salah. Should the prayer be repeated or only the sajdah? The answer depends on whether the addition is considered a nullifying act. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn), and Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
A person performs an invalid sajdah tilawah during prayer (e.g., reciting a non-sajdah verse). The sajdah is not valid but the prayer is in progress.
The cause of sajdah (hearing/reciting a sajdah verse) was not actually present, so the sajdah is invalid.
2
State the primary ruling (from the author)
The author says: repeat the sajdah (because its cause was mistakenly thought established) but do not repeat the prayer.
This is the position of the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf).
3
Identify the dissenting position
A narration in al-Nawadir states that the prayer becomes invalid because something not from the prayer was added. This is attributed to Imam Muhammad.
Nawadir are rare transmissions, less authoritative than zahir al-riwayah.
4
Analyze the reasoning of each side
Shaykhayn: prayer is invalidated only by omitting a pillar or bringing a contradictory act; sajdah is not contradictory. Imam Muhammad: any addition of an act not from the prayer invalidates, even if less than a rak'ah.
The key point is whether the addition is considered nullifying.
5
Examine the basis of difference
The dispute hinges on whether an addition of less than a full rak'ah can invalidate the prayer.
Shaykhayn: No; Imam Muhammad: Yes.
6
Determine the mufta bihi
The text presents the Shaykhayn's view as the primary ruling; it is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The Nawadir position is noted but not adopted as the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واعادوها لتفرد سببها ولم يعيدوا الصلوة لان مجرد السجدة لاينا [؟] في اجرم الصلوة وفي النوادرانها تفس [؟] لأنهم زادوا فيها ماليس منها وقيل هو قول محمد  ترجمہ مصنف نے کہا کہ اس سجدہ کا اعادہ کریں کیونکہ اس کا سبب ثابت ہو چکا ہے۔ اور نماز کا اعادہ نہ کریں اس لئے کہ محض سجدہ کرنا احرام نماز کے منافی نہیں ہے اور نوادر میں ہے کہ نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ ان لوگوں نے اپنی نماز میں ایسا سجدہ بڑھایا ہے جو نماز میں سے نہیں ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ یہ امام محمد کا قول ہے۔ تشریح صاحب کتاب کہتے ہیں کہ ان لوگوں نے نماز کے اندر جو سجدہ تلاوت کیا ہے چونکہ وہ شرعاً معتبر نہیں ہے اس لئے نماز کے بعد اس سجدہ کا اعادہ کریں کیونکہ سجدہ تلاوت کا سبب ( سماع) پایا گیا اور چونکہ نماز فاسد نہیں ہوئی اس لئے نماز کا اعادہ کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور نماز کا فاسد نہ ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ نماز یا تو فاسد ہوتی ہے کسی رکن کو ترک کرنے سے اور یا فاسد ہوتی ہے منافی نماز چیز پیش آنے سے اور یہاں دونوں باتیں نہیں پائی گئیں کیونکہ سجدہ نماز کے منافی نہیں ہے نوادر کی روایت یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں نماز فاسد؟ جائے گی کیونکہ ان لوگوں نے نماز کے اندر ایسی چیز کا اضافہ کیا ہے کہ جو نماز کے افعال سے نہیں ہے بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ نماز کا فاسد ہونا امام محمد کا قول ہے شیخین کے نزدیک اس صورت میں نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی بنیاد اختلاف یہ ہے کہ امام محمد کے نزدیک سجدہ کی زیادتی مفسد نماز ہے اور شیخین کے نزدیک ایک رکعت سے کم کی زیادتی نماز فاسد نہیں کرتی۔
He said: And they should repeat them (the sajdahs) because their cause is established, and they should not repeat the prayer because merely performing the sajdah does not contradict the inviolability of prayer. And in al-Nawadir, it is that it invalidates (the prayer) because they added to it something not from it, and it is said that this is the saying of Muhammad. Translation: The author said that they should repeat this sajdah because its cause has been established. And they should not repeat the prayer because merely performing sajdah is not contrary to the inviolability of prayer. And in Nawadir, it is that the prayer will become invalid because these people added to their prayer a sajdah that is not from the prayer. And it has been said that this is the saying of Imam Muhammad. Explanation: The author of the book says that since the sajdah tilawah that these people performed in prayer is not valid according to Shariah, they should repeat it after the prayer because the cause (hearing) was present. And since the prayer is not invalid, there is no need to repeat it. The reason the prayer is not invalid is that prayer is invalidated either by omitting a pillar or by the occurrence of something contradictory to prayer. Neither of these is found here because sajdah is not contradictory to prayer. The tradition in Nawadir is that in this case the prayer does become invalid because these people added to their prayer something not from its actions. Some say that the invalidity of the prayer is the saying of Imam Muhammad. According to the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani? Actually Shaykhayn refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf here? The text says Shaykhayn, meaning Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad differs), in this case the prayer does not become invalid. The basis of the difference is that according to Imam Muhammad, the addition of a sajdah invalidates the prayer, whereas according to the two shaykhs, adding less than a rak'ah does not invalidate the prayer.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect on prayer when a person performs an invalid sajdah tilawah during prayer. The author (al-Marghinani or the commentator) states that the sajdah must be repeated because its cause (hearing the verse) remains, but the prayer need not be repeated because simply prostrating does not contradict the state of prayer. However, a narration from al-Nawadir (the rare transmissions) reports that Imam Muhammad considers the prayer to be invalid because the addition of a sajdah that is not part of the prayer is a disruptive addition. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the prayer remains valid because adding less than a full rak'ah does not invalidate the prayer. The dispute hinges on whether the addition of a sajdah (which is less than a rak'ah) nullifies the prayer. The text indicates that the relied-upon position is that of the Shaykhayn.

Key Terms
نوادر (nawaadir): Rare or non-standard transmissions within the Hanafi school, as opposed to the zahir al-riwayah.
شیخین (shaykhayn): The two masters: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (in this context).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis of the dispute between the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad?
A) Whether the sajdah was validly intended
B) Whether an addition of less than a rak'ah invalidates the prayer
C) Whether the sajdah was performed at the correct time
D) Whether the cause of sajdah was present

Key Takeaway
In the relied-upon Hanafi position, adding an act less than a rak'ah (like an invalid sajdah) does not invalidate the prayer; only the sajdah is repeated.

Sajdah Wajib in Prayer Cannot Be Made Up Outside
Ruling on sajdah wajib in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a sajdah that becomes wajib during prayer cannot be performed outside prayer and explain the legal reason (talil) for this ruling.

Core Idea
A sajdah wajib in prayer is prayer-associated; it cannot be fulfilled outside.

This lesson addresses a specific ruling: if a sajdah tilawah becomes obligatory during the prayer, it must be performed within that prayer. If missed, it cannot be made up later. The reasoning (talil) is that the sajdah is integrated into the prayer's structure and shares its virtue. Understanding this distinction is important for proper performance of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Recognize the act in question: a sajdah (prostration) that becomes wajib during prayer due to recitation of a sajdah verse.
This is called sajdah tilawah, but only when it occurs during prayer.
2
State the Ruling
The ruling is that if this sajdah is not performed during the prayer, it cannot be performed outside of it. The text says: 'لم تقض خارج الصلوة' (it is not performed outside prayer).
This applies regardless of whether the omission was intentional or forgetful.
3
Understand the Reason (Talil)
The reason given is that the sajdah is 'salatiyyah' (prayer-associated) and has the virtue of the prayer itself. Performing it outside would be deficient because it lacks the full context of the prayer.
The term 'salatiyyah' highlights its integral connection to the prayer.
4
Apply the Distinction
Contrast this with a sajdah tilawah that becomes wajib outside prayer (e.g., reciting a sajdah verse while not praying). That sajdah can be performed later. The difference lies in the context of prayer.
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہر وہ سجدہ جو نماز میں واجب ہوا غیر نماز میں سجدہ کرنا کافی نہیں ہوگا ركل سجدة و جبت في الصلوة فلم يسجدها فيها لم تقض خارج الصلوة لانها صلاتية ولها مزية الصلوة لاتنا دى [؟] بالناقص  ترجمہ اور اگر وہ سجدہ جو نماز میں واجب ہوا ہے پھر اس کو نماز میں ادا نہ کیا تو پھر وہ نماز سے خارج میں ادا نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ سجدہ تو نماز کا و گیا [؟] ہے اور نماز کے سجدہ کو نماز کی فضیلت حاصل ہے تو وہ ناقص سے ادا نہ ہوگا۔
That sajdah which became wajib in prayer, performing it outside prayer is not sufficient. Every sajdah that became wajib in prayer, and he did not perform it in it, it is not performed outside prayer because it is a prayer-associated sajdah, and it has the virtue of prayer, so it is not fulfilled by the deficient. Translation: And if that sajdah which became wajib in prayer, then he did not perform it in the prayer, then it will not be performed outside the prayer. Because this sajdah has become part of the prayer, and the sajdah of prayer has the excellence of prayer, so it will not be fulfilled by the deficient.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This short passage establishes a rule: if a sajdah tilawah becomes obligatory during the prayer (e.g., the imam recites a sajdah verse within the prayer), it must be performed within that very prayer. If one neglects to perform it during the prayer, it cannot be made up outside the prayer by a separate prostration. The reason is that this sajdah is 'prayer-associated' (salatiyyah), meaning it is integrated into the prayer and has the special status of prayer acts. Since the prayer itself is a complete act, the sajdah must be performed with that completeness. Performing it outside would be deficient because it lacks the context of the prayer. This ruling contrasts with sajdah that becomes obligatory due to hearing outside prayer, which can be performed later.

Key Terms
صلاتیة (salatiyyah): Pertaining to prayer; a sajdah that is connected to the prayer and part of its acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an imam recites a sajdah verse during prayer and forgets to perform the sajdah, can he perform it after the prayer?
A) Yes, he can perform the sajdah after the prayer.
B) No, it cannot be performed outside because the sajdah is prayer-associated.
C) Yes, but only if he performs sajdah sahw as well.
D) No, prayer itself becomes invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
A sajdah that becomes wajib during prayer is prayer-associated and cannot be performed outside; it must be performed within its prayer context.

Joining Imam After Hearing Sajdah Ayah Outside Prayer
Ruling on hearing sajdah recitation outside prayer then joining imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on sajdat al-tilawah for a person who hears the ayah outside prayer and then joins the imam, and identify the condition that affects the obligation.

Core Idea
Hearing a sajdah ayah outside prayer obligates sajdah unless you later join the imam after he has already performed it — then the obligation drops due to catching the rak'ah.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from the Hanafi school: what happens when a person hears an imam recite a sajdah verse while he is not praying, and then decides to join the imam's prayer. The ruling depends on timing — whether he joins before or after the imam performs the sajdah. This is a nuance in the fiqh of sajdat al-tilawah that illustrates the interaction between individual obligation and following the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Sajdat al-tilawah is wajib upon hearing the sajdah ayah. The cause (sabab) is hearing the recitation.
This default applies when the person is not in prayer and does not join the imam.
2
Determine if the person joins the imam
The ruling changes if the person decides to join the congregation. The key variable is when he joins relative to the imam's sajdah.
3
Apply the first scenario: joins after the imam's sajdah
If he joins after the imam has performed the sajdah, he catches the rak'ah (becomes mudrik). The obligation is lifted because he is considered to have caught the sajdah with the imam.
This relies on the concept that catching the rak'ah includes catching the sajdah performed within it.
4
Apply the second scenario: joins before the imam's sajdah
If he joins before the imam performs the sajdah, he must perform it with the imam. This is because following the imam in sajdah is obligatory even without hearing the ayah.
The obligation is even stronger (اولیٰ) since he did hear the ayah.
5
Apply the third scenario: does not join
If he never joins the prayer, he must perform the sajdah alone, as the cause remains effective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قرأها الامام وسمعها رجل ليس معه فى الصلوة فدخل معه بعد ما سجدها الامام لم يكن عليه ان سجدها لانه صار مدر كالها بادراك الركعة وان دخل معه قبل ان يسجدها سجدها معه لانها لو لم سمعها سجدها معه فهنا اولى وان لم يدخل معه سجدها لتحقق السبب. تشریح: امام نے آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کی اور اس کو کسی ایسے آدمی نے سنا جو اس کے ساتھ نماز میں نہیں ہے۔ پھر امام کے سجدہ کرنے کے بعد وہ شخص امام کے ساتھ شامل ہو گیا تو اس پر سجدہ کرنا واجب نہ رہا۔ کیونکہ یہ شخص رکعت پانے سے سجدہ پانے والا ہو گیا اور اگر امام کے سجدہ کرنے سے پہلے وہ امام کے ساتھ داخل ہو گیا تو امام کے ساتھ سجدہ کرے کیونکہ اگر اس نے آیت سجدہ کو سنا بھی نہ ہوتا تو امام کے ساتھ اس پر سجدہ واجب ہوتا پس اب بدرجہ اولیٰ واجب ہے اور اگر وہ امام کے ساتھ داخل نہ ہو تو یہ سجدہ ادا کرے اس لئے کہ سبب متحقق ہوچکا ہے۔
If the imam recited [the sajdah ayah] and a man not in prayer heard it, then he joined the imam after the imam performed sajdah, he is not obligated to perform it, because he becomes a perceiver of it by catching the rak'ah. If he joined before the imam performed sajdah, he performs sajdah with him, because even if he had not heard it, he would perform sajdah with him; so here it is more appropriate. And if he does not join him, he performs it [alone] due to the existence of the cause.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for a person who hears an imam recite a sajdah verse while he himself is not in prayer, and then joins the imam later. There are two scenarios. First, if the person joins after the imam has already performed the sajdah of tilawah, the obligation of sajdah is lifted from this person because by catching the rak'ah (i.e., joining the prayer before the imam raises from ruku' of that rak'ah), he is considered to have caught the entire rak'ah including the sajdah. Second, if the person joins before the imam performs the sajdah, then he performs it with the imam; this is because even if he hadn't heard the ayah (e.g., if the imam recited quietly), joining the prayer would obligate him to follow the imam in sajdah. Since he heard the ayah, the obligation is even stronger (اولیٰ). If he never joins the prayer at all, he must perform the sajdah on his own, because the cause (hearing the sajdah ayah) has been established.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): The prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran where sajdah is prescribed.
مدرك (mudrik): A person who joins the imam during prayer, specifically catching the imam in a certain posture (here, catching the rak'ah).
سبب (sabab): Cause of obligation; for sajdat al-tilawah, the cause is reciting or hearing the sajdah verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hears the imam recite a sajdah ayah outside prayer, and then joins the imam after the imam has already performed the sajdah of tilawah, what is the ruling on the sajdah for this person?
A) He must perform sajdah immediately as a latecomer.
B) He does not have to perform sajdah because he caught the rak'ah.
C) He must perform sajdah after the prayer.
D) He must perform sajdah only if he heard the ayah while in prayer.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of sajdat al-tilawah for a listener outside prayer is removed if he joins the imam after the imam's sajdah and catches the rak'ah.

Salah — Prayer

6 min
Sajdah Obligatory in Prayer Cannot Be Made Up Outside
Ruling that sajdah owed during prayer cannot be performed after prayer ends

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a sajdah of tilawah missed during prayer cannot be performed outside and explain the proof based on the concept of maziyyat al-salah.

Core Idea
A sajdah owed during prayer has the complete merit of prayer and cannot be fulfilled by an incomplete act outside.

Sometimes during prayer, we recite or hear a verse of sajdah. This obligates a sajdah. But what if we forget to perform it and only remember after the prayer ends? The Hanafi school gives a clear ruling: it cannot be made up. This lesson unpacks the reasoning from Imam al-Quduri, focusing on the idea that acts within prayer have a special completeness that is lost outside.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sajdah tilawah that becomes obligatory during prayer. The ruling: if missed within prayer, it is not performed outside prayer; it is dropped.
This is a general principle (ضابطہ کلیہ) from Imam al-Quduri.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the principle that this sajdah has the 'merit of prayer' (مزية الصلوة). Prayer's merit makes the obligation complete (کامل واجب). A complete obligation cannot be fulfilled by an incomplete act (ناقص).
The 'incomplete act' refers to performing sajdah outside prayer without the surrounding prayer context.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The link between the principle and the ruling: the sajdah's obligation becomes complete within prayer because it partakes of prayer's merit. Outside prayer, the act lacks that merit, thus it is deficient. A deficient act cannot substitute for a complete obligation.
This is a deductive legal reasoning (talil) based on the nature of acts in prayer.
4
Note the scope and authority
The ruling applies to any sajdah tilawah that becomes obligatory during prayer. It is based on the authority of Imam al-Quduri (matn) and is part of the Hanafi corpus (zahir al-riwayah). There is no known intra-madhhab dispute on this specific point.
The commentary adds that the obligation is 'complete' (کامل واجب), so it cannot be dropped except by performing it within prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ركل سجدة و جبت في الصلوة فلم يسجدها فيها لم تقض خارج الصلوة لانها صلاتية ولها مزية الصلوة فلا تتادى بالناقص. ترجمہ: اور اگر وہ سجدہ جو نماز میں واجب ہوا ہے پھر اس کو نماز میں ادا نہ کیا تو پھر وہ نماز سے خارج میں ادا نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ سجدہ تو نماز کا ہو گیا ہے اور نماز کے سجدہ کو نماز کی فضیلت حاصل ہے تو وہ ناقص سے ادا نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح: صاحب قدوری نے ایک ضابطہ کلیہ کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ ہر وہ سجدہ جو نماز کے اندر آیت سجدہ تلاوت کرنے کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا لیکن نماز میں سجدہ نہیں کیا تو نماز سے باہر ادا کرنے سے ادا نہ ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ سجدہ نماز کا سجدہ ہے نماز کے افعال میں سے ہے اور نماز کے سجدہ کو نماز کی فضیلت حاصل ہے۔ اس لئے نماز کے اندر سجدہ تلاوت کا وجوب کامل ہوا اور جو چیز کامل واجب ہوتی ہے وہ ناقص کے ساتھ ادا نہیں ہوتی۔ اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ نماز سے باہر چونکہ نماز کی فضیلت نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے نماز سے باہر جو سجدہ ادا کیا جائے گا وہ ناقص ہوگا۔
Every sajdah that becomes obligatory in prayer and he does not perform it in it, it is not made up outside prayer because it is a prayer-related [sajdah] and it has the merit of prayer, so it is not fulfilled by an incomplete [act].
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage states a general principle (ضابطہ کلیہ) from Imam al-Quduri: If a sajdah of tilawah becomes obligatory during prayer (due to reciting or hearing a sajdah verse while in prayer), and the person neglects to perform it within the prayer, it cannot be performed later outside the prayer. The reason given is that this sajdah has the 'merit' or 'quality' (مزية) of prayer, meaning it is a complete act tied to the prayer's perfection. Performing it outside prayer is considered 'incomplete' (ناقص) because it lacks the surrounding prayer context. In Hanafi usul, an obligation that is attained in a complete manner cannot be fulfilled by an inferior substitute. Therefore, the sajdah is forfeited and not made up. The Urdu commentary explains that the obligation in prayer is complete (کامل واجب), and what is complete cannot be fulfilled by an incomplete act.

Key Terms
مزية (maziyyah): Distinctive merit or superiority; here, the special quality of prayer that makes the sajdah more complete.
ناقص (nāqiṣ): Deficient or incomplete act; an act lacking the full merit of the original context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Perform sajdah immediately after the prayer.
B) Perform sajdah after the prayer with takbir and salam.
C) The sajdah is waived and cannot be made up.
D) He must repeat the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
A sajdah of tilawah missed during prayer is forfeited and cannot be performed outside due to the complete merit of prayer.

One Sajdah for Two Recitations in Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sufficiency of one sajdah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on one sajdah sufficing for two recitations, distinguish the Nawadir narration, and apply the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
One sajdah in prayer suffices for pre-prayer and in-prayer recitations because the prayer sajdah is stronger.

Imagine you recite a sajdah verse outside prayer but forget to perform the sajdah. Then you begin your salah and recite the same verse again. During the prayer, you perform the sajdah of tilawah. Do you need to perform another sajdah after the prayer for the first recitation? This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue, exploring the main position and a less authoritative narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two recitations of the same sajdah verse: one outside prayer with no sajdah performed, and one inside prayer with sajdah performed. Determine if one sajdah can cover both.
The recitation inside prayer is the same verse as outside.
2
State the main Hanafi position
The main position (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that one sajdah in prayer suffices for both recitations.
3
Understand the reasoning
The prayer sajdah is stronger because of its connection to the prayer and its purpose (ittiṣāl al-maqṣūd), subsuming the earlier obligation.
The second sajdah is 'prayer-sajdah' (صلاتية), making the first follow.
4
Recognize the Nawadir narration
A less authoritative transmission (al-Nawadir) says a second sajdah after prayer is needed due to the strength of precedence (quwwat al-sabaq).
This is not the relied-upon view.
5
Apply the tarjih principle
The main position is mufta bihi because it comes from Zahir al-Riwayah, and the reasoning of strength of connection outweighs precedence.
The Nawadir narration is weaker and not followed in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من تلا سجدة فلم يسجدها حتى دخل في صلوة فاعادها وسجد اجزاته السجدة عن التلاوتين لان الثانية صلاتية فاستتبعت الأولى و فى النوادر يسجد اخرى بعد الفراغ لان للاولى قوة السبق قلنا للثانية قوة اتصال المقصود فترجحت بها. ترجمہ: اور جس شخص نے آیت سجدہ کو تلاوت کیا پھر اس کو ادا نہ کیا یہاں تک کہ کسی نماز میں داخل ہوا پھر اسی آیت سجدہ کو دوبارہ پڑھا اور سجدہ کیا تو یہ سجدہ اس کو دونوں تلاوتوں سے کافی ہو گیا کیونکہ دوسرا سجدہ تو اقوی ہے اس لئے کہ وہ نماز کا سجدہ ہے پس وہ پہلے سجدہ کو تابع بنانے والا ہو گیا اور نوادر میں ہے کہ دوسرا سجدہ نماز سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد کرے کیونکہ پہلے سجدہ کو تقدم کی قوت حاصل ہے اس لئے بات واضح ہے کہ سجدے برابر ہو گئے ہم جواب دیتے ہیں کہ دوسرے سجدہ کو مقصود سے متصل ہونے کی قوت حاصل ہے اس لئے دوسرے سجدہ کو ترجیح ہوگئی۔
Whoever recites a sajdah [verse] and does not perform sajdah until he enters into prayer, then he repeats it [the ayah] and performs sajdah, that sajdah suffices for both recitations because the second is a prayer-sajdah, so it makes the first follow. And in al-Nawadir: he performs another after finishing because the first has the strength of precedence. We say: the second has the strength of connection to the intended purpose, so it outweighs.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where a person recites a sajdah verse outside prayer but does not perform the sajdah. Then he enters prayer and recites the same verse again, and within the prayer he performs the sajdah of tilawah. The ruling according to the main Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that this single sajdah suffices for both recitations. The reasoning is that the second sajdah (performed in prayer) is stronger (اقوی) because it has the merit of prayer, and thus it subsumes the first obligation. However, there is a narration in al-Nawadir (a collection of rare transmissions) that says he should perform another sajdah after finishing the prayer, because the first recitation had the strength of precedence. The Hanafi response is that the second sajdah's strength lies in its connection to the intended purpose (اتصال المقصود), i.e., its immediate performance in prayer, which gives it preference. So the relied-upon position is that one sajdah suffices.

Key Terms
النوادر (al-nawādir): A collection of rare or less authoritative transmissions within the Hanafi school, not part of the six major books (Zahir al-Riwayah).
قوة السبق (quwwat al-sabaq): The strength of being earlier in time, giving a kind of precedence that might require separate fulfillment.
اتصال المقصود (ittiṣāl al-maqṣūd): Connection to the intended purpose; here, the second sajdah is performed immediately when the purpose (sajdah) is intended, giving it strength.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must perform separate sajdahs for each recitation.
B) One sajdah in prayer suffices for both.
C) He must perform one sajdah outside prayer first, then another inside.
D) He must perform a sajdah after prayer for the first recitation.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a single sajdah performed in prayer suffices for both recitations, due to the strength of the prayer sajdah.

One Sajda Tilawa Covers Two Recitations When Second is in Prayer
Explains that one sajda in prayer suffices for two recitations when second is in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that one sajda tilawa performed inside prayer suffices for both an outside and inside recitation, and apply the principle of tadakhul to related scenarios.

Core Idea
One sajda inside prayer covers two recitations because the stronger prayer-prostration subsumes the weaker.

This lesson explores a practical scenario where a person recites a sajda verse outside prayer, then again inside prayer, and performs one sajda in prayer. The Hidayah explains why that single sajda fulfills both obligations, based on a key Hanafi principle called tadakhul (merging). Understanding this helps avoid unnecessary repetition in worship and clarifies the school's preference for ease.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Question
Recognize the sequence: first recitation outside prayer (no prostration), then second recitation inside prayer, followed by a prostration inside. The question is whether that one prostration covers both recitations.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling and Principle
The Hanafi relied-upon ruling is that one sajda suffices for both. The underlying principle is tadakhul (merging) applied to acts of worship, where a stronger act can fulfill the obligation of a weaker one.
Tadakhul is a key Hanafi concept to avoid hardship.
3
Follow the Proof (Dalil Aqli)
The reasoning is rational: the prostration inside prayer is complete and strong because it gains virtue from the prayer itself. A prostration outside is incomplete. Therefore, the stronger second subsumes the weaker first.
The strength comes from the prayer context.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Disagreement
In al-Nawadir, a non-standard transmission, it is reported that one should prostrate again after prayer because the first outside recitation has precedence in time. This view gives weight to the obligation of the first recitation.
This is from Imam Muhammad's narration via Hasan ibn Ziyad.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih (Preference)
The Hidayah prefers the Zahir al-Riwayah view: the second prostration is stronger due to its connection to the intended purpose (recitation within prayer), so no extra prostration is needed. This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
The principle of tadakhul and preference for the stronger act avoids hardship.

Explanation: The author of al-Quduri pointed to a general principle: Every prostration that becomes obligatory due to reciting an aya of prostration outside of prayer, but one did not prostrate during the prayer, then performing it outside the prayer will not fulfill it. The proof is that this prostration, because it is a prostration of prayer, means that the recitation of the aya of prostration which necessitates prostration is among the acts of prayer, and the prostration of prayer has the virtue of prayer. Therefore, the obligation of the prostration of recitation within prayer is complete, and what becomes completely obligatory cannot be performed with an incomplete [act]. It is obvious that outside of prayer, since the virtue of prayer is absent, the prostration performed outside will be incomplete. If one recited an aya of prostration and did not prostrate, then entered prayer and recited the same aya again and prostrated, this prostration will suffice for both recitations. Translation: And if one does... because the second would necessitate precedence of the ruling over the cause. 'Whoever recited an aya of prostration and did not prostrate until he entered into prayer and repeated it and prostrated, this prostration suffices for the two recitations because the second, being a prayer-prostration, subsumes the first.' And in al-Nawadir: 'He should prostrate another after finishing because the first has the strength of precedence.' We say: 'The second has the strength of connection to the intended purpose, so it is given preference.' This passage discusses the merging (tadakhul) of prostration of recitation. The issue: If someone recited an aya of prostration outside prayer and did not perform it until he entered into some nafl or fard prayer, then recited the same aya again and performed the prostration within the prayer, it will suffice for both. The proof is that the second prostration is stronger, and it is stronger because it is a prayer-prostration. Since the second prostration is stronger, the first which became obligatory outside prayer is subordinate to it, and because the superordinate includes the subordinate, the second prostration includes the first. He went and returned... merging (tadakhul) to avoid hardship.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Hidayah explaining a ruling about prostration of recitation (sajda tilawa). It states a general principle: if a prostration becomes obligatory outside prayer due to recitation, but one does not perform it, then later performs it inside prayer after reciting again, the prostration inside suffices for both recitations. The reasoning is that the prostration inside prayer is complete and strong because it is connected to the prayer's virtue, whereas a prostration outside is incomplete. Therefore, the second prostration subsumes the first. The commentator also mentions a differing view from al-Nawadir (transmitted from Imam Muhammad) that one should perform an additional prostration after finishing prayer because the first recitation has the strength of precedence. However, the preferred view (given in the Hidayah) is that the second prostration is stronger because of its connection to the intended act (recitation within prayer), so no additional prostration is needed. This illustrates the Hanafi principle of tadakhul (merging) for acts of worship to avoid hardship.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadakhul): The legal principle that a single act can fulfill the obligation of multiple causes when the acts are of the same type and occur within a single context (like one prostration for multiple recitations).
سجدہ تلاوت (sajda tilawa): The prostration required upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of prostration in the Quran.
نوادر (nawadir): Rare or non-standard transmissions from the early Hanafi imams, not part of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
One sajda tilawa performed inside prayer suffices for both an outside and inside recitation because the stronger prayer-prostration subsumes the weaker, applying tadakhul.

Sajda Tilawa: New Recitation After Fulfilled Obligation Requires New Prostration
States that a second recitation after a performed prostration requires a new prostration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a sajda verse is recited again after the prostration has already been performed, and explain the rational proof that prevents tadakhul.

Core Idea
A fulfilled obligation cannot be reused for a new cause—the ruling cannot precede its cause.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in sajda tilawa: what happens when you recite a sajda verse outside prayer, perform the prostration, and then recite the same verse again inside prayer? The Hanafi school rules that a new prostration is wajib. The proof is a rational one based on the logical order of cause and effect, preventing any merger (tadakhul) of obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal question
First, understand the factual situation: someone recites a sajda verse outside prayer, prostrates, then recites the same verse in prayer. The question is whether the first prostration suffices for the second recitation or a new prostration is required.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to the Hanafi school, a new prostration is obligatory (wajib). The first does not cover the second recitation.
This ruling is based on zahir al-riwayah and is mufta bihi.
3
Understand the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The proof is that if we were to attach the second recitation to the first prostration, it would mean the ruling (prostration) preceded its cause (recitation), which is rationally impossible. The cause must come before the ruling.
This principle is derived from the necessity of cause and effect in legal rulings.
4
Apply the principle of tadakhul
Tadakhul (merger) only applies when both causes are still outstanding at the time of performing the act. Here, the first obligation was already fulfilled, so merger is impossible. Thus the second recitation creates a new, separate wajib.
This distinguishes the case from the earlier ruling where the first prostration was not performed and tadakhul applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He recited an aya of prostration, then prostrated. Then in prayer he recited the aya of prostration again. Now the first prostration is not sufficient. 'If he recited and prostrated then entered into prayer and recited it, he should prostrate for it because the second is the one that subsumes, and there is no way to attach it to the first because that would lead to the ruling preceding the cause.' Translation: And if outside prayer he recited and prostrated, then entered prayer and recited that aya of prostration, then he must prostrate for it because the second prostration is the subsuming one, and there is no reason to attach it to the first, because that would cause the ruling to precede the cause. Explanation: The issue is that if someone recited an aya of prostration outside prayer and performed the prostration, then entered prayer and recited the same aya again, then a prostration of recitation becomes obligatory due to the recitation inside prayer. The proof is that it passed in the first issue that the second prostration is stronger because it is a prayer-prostration, and due to being stronger, it subsumes the first prostration. But when the second prostration is the subsumer of the first, there is no reason to attach the second prostration to the first. Because if the second prostration were attached to the first, it would mean that for the second prostration, the recitation occurred later but the prostration was performed earlier. And it is clear that the cause of the obligation of prostration is recitation. So in this case, it would necessitate the cause being delayed and the ruling being advanced, which is not correct. Thus it is established that in this case, tadakhul is impossible. And since tadakhul is impossible, the second prostration is obligatory due to the second recitation.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage presents a second ruling about sajda tilawa. Unlike the previous case where the first prostration was not performed, here the person has already performed the prostration outside prayer. Then they enter prayer and recite the same aya again. The question is whether the previous prostration suffices for the second recitation. The answer is no; a new prostration is required. The reasoning is that the second recitation is a new cause of obligation. If we tried to attach the second recitation to the first prostration, it would imply that the ruling (prostration) preceded its cause (recitation), which is logically impossible. The principle of tadakhul does not apply here because the first obligation was already fulfilled. Therefore, the second recitation creates a new wajib for a new prostration. This distinction shows that tadakhul only operates when both causes remain unfulfilled at the time of performing the act; once fulfilled, later causes require separate acts.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause of obligation; here, recitation of an aya of sajda is the cause for the obligation of sajda.
حکم (hukm): The legal ruling; here, the obligation to prostrate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone recites a sajda verse outside prayer and performs the prostration, then later in prayer recites the same verse again, what is the ruling?
A) No prostration is needed because the first already fulfilled the obligation.
B) A new prostration is required for the second recitation.
C) One prostration suffices for both because the second is in prayer.
D) The first prostration becomes void and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Once an obligation is fulfilled, a new identical cause creates a new obligation; the principle of tadakhul does not operate when the first obligation is already discharged.
