اگر قصر کے بجائے اتمام کیا تو کیا حکم ہے
وإن صلى أربعا وقعد في الثانية قدر التشهد أجزأته الأوليان عن الفرض والأخريان له نافلة اعتبارا بالفجر وذلك يأثم ويصير مسيئا لتأخير السلام وإن لم يقعد في الثانية قدرها بطلت لاختلاط الناقلة بها قبل إكمال أركانها وهو مأثور.
ترجمہ: اور اگر مسافر نے چار رکعتیں پڑھیں اور دوسری رکعت پر تشہد کی مقدار پر بیٹھ گیا تو پہلی دو رکعتیں فرض سے اس کو کافی ہو جائیں گی اور بعد کی دو رکعتیں اس کے لئے نفل ہوں گی فجر پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور تاخیر سلام کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوگا۔ اور اگر دوسری رکعت پر بقدر تشہد نہیں بیٹھا تو یہ نماز باطل ہوگئی کیونکہ نفل فرض کے ساتھ اس کے ارکان مکمل ہونے سے پہلے مخلوط ہو گیا۔
تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مسافر نے بجائے دو رکعت کے چار رکعت پڑھیں اور تشہد کی مقدار دوسری رکعت پر بیٹھ بھی گیا تو پہلی دو رکعتیں فرض اور بعد کی دو رکعتیں نفل شمار ہوں گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فجر کی نماز پر قیاس کیا ہے یعنی اگر فجر کی چار رکعتیں پڑھیں اور دوسری رکعت پر بیٹھ گیا تو فجر کی دو رکعت فرض ادا ہو جائیں گی۔ البتہ سلام میں تاخیر کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوگا۔ اور اگر یہ مسافر دوسری رکعت پر تشہد کی مقدار نہیں بیٹھا تو اس کی نماز باطل ہو جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ارکان فرض مکمل ہونے سے پہلے فرض کے ساتھ نفل مخلوط ہو گیا۔ ارکان اس لئے مکمل نہیں ہوئے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ جو رکن ہے اس کو ترک کر دیا۔ اور فرض کے ارکان مکمل ہونے سے پہلے فرض کو نفل کے ساتھ مخلوط کر دینا مبطل صلوٰۃ ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی نماز باطل ہوگئی۔
If he prays four rak'ahs and sits in the second rak'ah for the amount of tashahhud, the first two suffice him for the fard, and the last two are nafl for him, by analogy to Fajr. And that is, he commits a sin and becomes an offender because of delaying the salam. And if he does not sit in the second rak'ah for the amount of tashahhud, the prayer becomes invalid because of mixing the nafl with it (the fard) before completing its pillars. And this is transmitted.
Translation: And if the traveler prays four rak'ahs and sits in the second rak'ah for the amount of tashahhud, then the first two rak'ahs suffice for the fard, and the last two are nafl for him, by analogy to Fajr. And due to delaying the salam, he becomes sinful. And if he does not sit in the second rak'ah for the amount of tashahhud, then his prayer becomes invalid because the nafl mixed with the fard before its pillars were completed.
Clarification: The issue is that if the traveler prays four rak'ahs instead of two, and he does sit in the second rak'ah for the amount of tashahhud, then the first two rak'ahs are considered fard and the last two are nafl. The author of al-Hidayah analogized it to the Fajr prayer: i.e., if one prays four rak'ahs for Fajr and sits in the second rak'ah, the two rak'ahs of Fajr fard are performed. However, he becomes sinful for delaying the salam. And if this traveler does not sit in the second rak'ah for the amount of tashahhud, then his prayer becomes invalid. The proof is that the nafl was mixed with the fard before the completion of its pillars. The pillars were not completed because the final sitting, which is a pillar, was omitted. And mixing the fard with nafl before completing its pillars nullifies the prayer. Therefore his prayer is invalid.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the consequence when a traveler, instead of performing qasr (two rak'ahs), prays four rak'ahs. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios:

1. If the traveler sits in the second rak'ah for the duration of tashahhud, then the first two rak'ahs count as the obligatory fard, and the last two rak'ahs are considered supererogatory (nafl). This is by analogy to the Fajr prayer: if someone prays four rak'ahs for Fajr and sits in the second, the first two are Fajr fard and the last two are nafl. However, because the traveler delayed the final salam (which should come after two rak'ahs), he commits a sin (ithm) for the delay, but the prayer is valid.

2. If the traveler does not sit in the second rak'ah (i.e., he stands up for the third without pausing for tashahhud), the prayer becomes invalid (batil). The reason is that the nafl (the last two rak'ahs) becomes mixed with the fard before the fard's pillars are complete. The missing pillar is the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah), which is a rukn. Without completing the fard's pillars, mixing it with nafl nullifies the prayer. Therefore, the traveler's prayer is batil and must be repeated.

The proof is explicit: the analogy to Fajr is drawn from the same ruling. The key condition for the prayer to be valid (though sinful) is the sitting for tashahhud in the second rak'ah. This distinguishes between a valid but sin-inducing prayer and a completely invalid one.

Key Terms
اتمام (itmam): Performing the full four rak'ahs instead of shortening to two.
قعدة (qa'dah): The sitting posture in prayer, especially the sitting after the second rak'ah.
تشهد (tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith during the sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a traveler prays four rak'ahs for Zuhr and sits for tashahhud in the second rak'ah, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is batil (invalid).
B) The first two rak'ahs count as fard and the last two as nafl, and he is sinful for delaying salam.
C) The prayer is valid and no sin.
D) The entire prayer counts as fard.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a traveler who prays four rak'ahs must sit for tashahhud in the second rak'ah for the prayer to be valid; otherwise it is invalid.

When Qasr Begins: Leaving the City Boundary
Specifies the point at which qasr becomes applicable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the legal boundary (shart) for the obligation of qasr according to the Hanafi school and explain the ta'lil (legal reasoning) based on the definition of residence.

Core Idea
Until you exit the built-up area of your city, you are a resident — qasr begins only when you leave the houses behind.

One of the first questions a traveler faces is when to start shortening prayers. The Hanafi school gives a clear, practical criterion: qasr begins when you leave the houses of your city (misl). This short passage from al-Hidayah presents the ruling, its logical underpinning, and a companion tradition to support it. Mastering this boundary ensures your qasr is valid from its proper beginning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the act of shortening prayer (qasr) during travel. It states that when a traveler leaves the houses of the city, he should pray two rak'ahs (i.e., shorten). This tells us that qasr becomes obligatory at that point.
The ruling is that qasr is wajib for the traveler, but the passage focuses on when it starts.
2
Locate the condition (shart) for qasr
The condition mentioned is 'leaving the houses of the city' (مفارقة بيوت المصر). The traveler must physically exit the built-up area for the concession to take effect.
Houses (بيوت) here means the entire inhabited area, not just one's own home.
3
Understand the ta'lil (legal reasoning)
The reason given is that residence (iqamah) is tied to entering the houses, so travel (safar) is tied to leaving them. This is a logical inversion: if entering makes you a resident, then leaving makes you a traveler.
This ta'lil is based on the definitional link between residence and the city.
4
Examine the supporting evidence
The author cites an athar from Ali (RA): 'If we pass this wall (khus), we would shorten.' This indicates that the Companions took the physical boundary of the city as the point for qasr.
The word 'khus' may refer to a wall or cluster of houses marking the city limit.
5
Apply the concept
Before leaving the built-up area, one is a resident (muqim) and must pray complete prayers. After leaving, one becomes a traveler (musafir) and must shorten four-rak'ah prayers. This applies at the start of the outward journey and also when returning.
The same rule applies when returning: when you re-enter the city houses, you become a resident again.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قصر نماز کہاں سے شروع کرے
وإذا فارق المسافر بيوت المصر صلى ركعتين لأن الإقامة تتعلق بدخولها فيتعلق السفر بالخروج منها. وفيه الأثر عن علي رضي الله عنه: لو جاوزنا هذا الخص لقصرنا.
ترجمہ: اور جب مسافر نے شہر کے گھروں کو چھوڑا تو دو رکعت پڑھے کیونکہ اقامت (کا حکم) ان گھروں کے اندر داخل ہونے سے متعلق ہے تو سفر کا حکم ان سے نکلنے سے متعلق ہوگا۔
Where does qasr begin? And when the traveler leaves the houses of the city, he prays two rak'ahs, because residence is tied to entering them, so travel is tied to leaving them. And in it is the athar from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'If we pass this wall/cluster, we would shorten.'
Translation: And when the traveler leaves the houses of the city, he prays two rak'ahs, because residence (iqama) is tied to entering them, so travel is tied to leaving them.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This short passage states the Hanafi ruling on when the concession of qasr begins for a traveler. The criterion is leaving the built-up area of the city (misl). The reasoning is that residence (iqama) is legally established by entering the city limits, and travel is established by leaving them. The author supports this with an athar (tradition) from Ali ibn Abi Talib (may Allah be pleased with him) saying that if they passed a certain wall (khus), they would pray qasr. This indicates that the boundary of the city is the point at which the rules of travel begin. Therefore, before leaving the inhabited buildings, a person is considered a resident (muqim) and must pray complete prayers. Once he has left the city houses, he becomes a traveler (musafir) and must pray qasr for the four-rak'ah prayers. This is the standard Hanafi position.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): The city or town; the inhabited area with buildings.
اقامت (iqamah): Residence; the legal status of being a resident (muqim) requiring full prayer.
سفر (safar): Travel; the legal status of being a traveler (musafir) entitling one to qasr.
خص (khus): A wall or cluster of houses marking the boundary of the built-up area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) As soon as the traveler leaves his house.
B) When the traveler leaves the houses of the city (built-up area).
C) After traveling one mile.
D) When the traveler reaches his destination.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that qasr begins when the traveler leaves the built-up area (houses) of his city, based on the principle that residence is defined by entry and travel by exit.

The Hanafi Ruling on Qasr: Wajib or Mubah? An Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Hanafi argues qasr is wajib against Shafi'i view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that qasr is wajib and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Qasr is wajib because the imperative 'accept' and the nature of charity as relinquishment make rejection impossible.

This passage presents the Hanafi school's argument against the Shafi'i view that shortening prayer while travelling is merely permissible. The Hanafis use two main proofs: the Quranic use of 'la junah' to indicate obligation in the context of Sa'i, and the hadith's imperative 'faqbilu' which, combined with the nature of qasr as a relinquishment-type charity, makes it obligatory. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to see how different usul principles yield different rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
Determine the exact issue: the legal status of qasr (shortening prayer) while travelling. The Hanafi school holds it is wajib; the Shafi'i school says it is mubah.
This is a well-known ikhtilaf in salah rulings.
2
Analyse the Hanafi proof from the Quran
Examine how the Hanafi author uses the Sa'i verse (Quran 2:158) to argue that 'la junah' can indicate obligation. Even Imam al-Shafi'i accepts that Sa'i is wajib, showing the phrase does not always mean permissibility.
Focus on the contextual usage within a religious rite.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof from the hadith
Look at the hadith of Umar where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'faqbilu' (accept) the charity of qasr. In Hanafi usul, an imperative indicates obligation (wujub).
The imperative 'faqbilu' is the key linguistic element.
4
Understand the isqat/tamlik distinction
Learn the Hanafi classification of charity into tamlikat (transfer of ownership, rejectable) and isqatat (relinquishment, not rejectable). Qasr is isqat-type, so rejection does not nullify it, hence it becomes obligatory.
This is a distinctive Hanafi legal reasoning.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: Hanafis must shorten when traveling; Shafi'is may choose. This affects the validity and sinfulness of the act.
The difference is in whether leaving qasr is a sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تسلیم کر لیا جائے کہ آیت میں اصل نماز کا قصر مراد ہے تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ امام شافعی کا یہ کہنا کہ لفظ لا جناح اباحت کے لئے ذکر کیا جاتا ہے متعلق ہوتا ۔ وجوب کے لئے نہیں غلط ہے کیونکہ آیت إِنَّ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةَ مِنْ شَعَائِرِ اللهِ فَمَنْ حَجَّ الْبَيْتَ أَوِ اعْتَمَرَ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَطَّوَّفَ بِهِمَا میں لا جناح سے کی بین الصفاء المروۃ کے وجوب کو ذکر کیا گیا ہے۔ خود امام شافعی بھی اس موقع پر اباحت مراد نہیں لیتے تشریح قصر پڑھنا واج جیسا کہ جلالین میں مذکور ہے۔ امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ حدیث عمر کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ حدیث ہماری دلیل ہے نہ کہ آپ کی اس لئے کہ حدیث کے اندر فاقبلو امر کا اس آبادی - صیغہ ہے اور امر وجوب کے لئے آتا ہے پس قصرہ جس کو صدقہ کہا گیا ہے اس کا قبول کرنا واجب ہوانہ کہ مباح دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ صدقہ لقصرنا خصر دو طرح کا ہوتا ہے ایک تملیکات کے قبیلہ سے جیسے مال کا صدقہ دوم اسقاطات کے قبیلہ سے جیسے عتاق ( آزاد کرنا ) اور قصاص کو معاف نماز قصر پڑھیں کرنا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جو صدقہ تملیکات کے قبیلہ سے ہوا گر اس کو رد کر دیا جائے تو وہ رد ہو جائے گا۔ البتہ جو اسقاطات کے قبیلہ سے ہو درد کرنے سے رد نہیں ہوتا۔ پس قصر صلوۃ ایسا صدقہ ہے جواز قبیل اسقاطات ہے۔ لہذا یہ رد کرنے سے رد نہیں ہوگا اور جب متصدق علیہ کے رد کرنے سے رد نہیں ہوا تو گویا واجب ہوا ۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ قصر واجب ہے۔
It should be accepted that the verse means shortening the original prayer. We say that Imam Shafi'i's statement that the word 'la junah' is used for permissibility, not for obligation, is wrong because in the verse 'Indeed, as-Safa and al-Marwah are among the symbols of Allah. So whoever makes Hajj to the House or performs 'umrah, there is no blame upon him for walking between them,' obligation of the sa'i between Safa and Marwah is mentioned with 'la junah'. Imam Shafi'i himself does not take it as permissibility there. Explanation: Qasr is wajib, as mentioned in Jalalayn. The answer to the hadith of Umar presented by Imam Shafi'i is that this hadith is our evidence, not yours, because in the hadith the imperative form 'faqbilu' is used, and an imperative indicates obligation. So accepting the charity (qasr) is wajib, not mubah. A second answer is that sadaqah (charity) is of two types: one from the category of transferring ownership (tamlikat) like charity of wealth, and the second from the category of relinquishments (isqatat) like manumission and forgiving retaliation. The rule is that a charity from the category of tamlikat, if it is rejected, it is rejected. But a charity from the category of isqatat is not rejected by rejection. So the shortening of prayer is a charity from the category of isqatat. Therefore it is not rejected by rejection, and since it is not rejected by the rejection of the recipient, it becomes obligatory. Thus it is proven that qasr is wajib.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is on whether shortening prayer (qasr) while travelling is wajib (obligatory) or mubah (permissible). The author first refutes the Shafi'i claim that the Quranic phrase 'la junah' (no blame) indicates permissibility, citing the verse about Sa'i between Safa and Marwah where 'la junah' is used for an obligatory act, and even Shafi'is consider that wajib. Then he addresses the Shafi'i proof from the hadith of Umar where the Prophet said 'Faqbilu' (accept) the charity of qasr. The Hanafi response is twofold: firstly, the imperative form 'faqbilu' indicates obligation (wujub) per Hanafi usul; secondly, the charity here is of the type isqatat (relinquishment) which is not nullified by rejection, unlike tamlikat (transfer of ownership). Since the recipient (the traveler) cannot reject it, it becomes obligatory. Therefore qasr is wajib according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rak'ah prayer to two rak'ahs while travelling.
لا جناح (la junah): No sin/blame; used in Quran to indicate permissibility or obligation contextually.
صدقہ (sadaqah): Charity; here metaphorically for the concession of qasr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what type of charity is qasr, and what does that imply for its ruling?
A) Tamlik-type charity; it can be rejected so qasr is mubah
B) Isqat-type charity; it cannot be rejected so qasr is wajib
C) Isqat-type charity; it is optional like manumission
D) Tamlik-type charity; it is impermissible to reject

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school deems qasr wajib because the imperative in the hadith and the nature of isqat charity indicate obligation, contrary to the Shafi'i view that it is merely permissible.

Ruling on a Traveler Who Mistakenly Prays Four Rak'ahs
Rules for when a traveler mistakenly prays four rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two possible rulings for a traveler who prays four rak'ahs instead of two, identify the condition that determines which ruling applies, and apply the underlying qiyas and talil to new scenarios.

Core Idea
If a traveler sits for tashahhud in the second rak'ah, the first two count as fard; if not, the prayer is invalid.

When a traveler intends to shorten the prayer (qasr) from four to two rak'ahs, but mistakenly prays four, the validity of his prayer depends on whether he sat for tashahhud in the second rak'ah. The Hanafi school provides a detailed ruling based on analogy with Fajr prayer and the principle that mixing voluntary acts before completing the obligatory pillars invalidates the prayer. This lesson unpacks both scenarios and their legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the traveler's default obligation
A traveler is required to shorten the 4-rak'ah prayers to 2 rak'ahs (qasr). Praying 4 is a mistake.
The fard is 2 rak'ahs.
2
Recognize the two scenarios
The author presents two cases: (a) the traveler sits for tashahhud in the second rak'ah, (b) he does not sit in the second rak'ah.
3
Analyze the first scenario: sitting at second
If he sits in the second rak'ah for the duration of tashahhud, the first two rak'ahs are valid as fard, and the last two become nafl. This is analogous to someone praying 4 rak'ahs for Fajr—the first two suffice for Fajr.
He commits a sin by delaying the salutation.
4
Analyze the second scenario: no sitting at second
If he does not sit in the second rak'ah for tashahhud, the prayer is invalid. The reason is that the extra rak'ahs (nafl) become mixed with the fard before its pillars are complete. The final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) is a pillar of the fard, and without it the fard is incomplete.
Mixing nafl with incomplete fard invalidates the prayer.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Consider a traveler who prays 4 rak'ahs for Maghrib (which is 3 rak'ahs) – this analogy would need careful adjustment. The principle is that the fard must be completed before adding voluntary acts.
This lesson focuses on the 4-rak'ah prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر قصر کے بجائے اتمام کیا تو کیا حکم ہے اربعا والعص پڑھیں اور عصر ولا يزال عن وان صلى اربعا وقعد فى الثانية قدر التشهد اجزاته الاوليان عن الفرض والاخريان له نافلة اعتبارا بالفجر ذلك قص ويصير مسينا لتأخير السلام وان لم يقعد فى الثانية قدرها بطلت لاختلاط الناقلة بها قبل اكمال اركانها وهو ماثور ترجمہ اور اگر مسافر نے چار رکعتیں پڑھیں اور دوسری رکعت پر تشہد کی مقدار پر بیٹھ گیا تو پہلی دو رکعتیں فرض سے اس کو کافی ہو جائیں الاقامة في ا گی اور بعد کی دور کعتیں اس کے لئے نفل ہوں گی فجر پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور تاخیر سلام کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوگا۔ اور اگر دوسری رکعت پر ترجمہ اور بقدر تشہد نہیں بیٹا تو یہ نماز باطل ہوگئی کیونکہ نفل، فرض کے ساتھ اس کے ارکان مکمل ہونے سے پہلے مخلوط ہو گیا۔ سے کم کی نیت تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مسافر نے بجائے دور کعت کے چار رکعت پڑھیں اور تشہد کی مقدار دوسری رکعت پر بیٹھ بھی گیا تو پہلی نے مدت اقام دور رکعتیں فرض اور بعد کی دورکعتیں نفل شمار ہوں گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فجر کی نماز پر قیاس کیا ہے یعنی اگر فجر کی چار رکعتیں پڑھیں اور دوسری رکعت پر بیٹھ گیا تو فجر کی دورکعت فرض ادا ہو جائیں گی۔ البتہ سلام میں تاخیر کی وجہ سے گنہگار ہوگا۔ اور اگر یہ مسافر دوسری رکعت پر اشارہ کرتا ہے تشہد کی مقدار نہیں بیٹھا تو اس کی نماز باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ارکان فرض مکمل ہونے سے پہلے فرض کے ساتھ فل مخلوط ہو گیا تشریح ہے۔ ارکان اس لئے مکمل نہیں ہوئے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ جور کن ہے اس کو ترک کر دیا۔ اور فرض کے ارکان مکمل ہونے سے پہلے فرض کو فل کے کرے پس جا ساتھ مخلوط کر دینا مبطل صلوٰۃ ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی نماز باطل ہوگئی ۔ دن سے کم ٹھہر
What is the ruling if one completes (four) instead of qasr? And if he prayed four and sat in the second [rak'ah] to the extent of tashahhud, the first two suffice for the fard and the last two are nafl for him, by analogy with Fajr. And he becomes sinful due to delaying the salutation. And if he did not sit in the second to the extent of tashahhud, it becomes invalid because the nafl is mixed with the fard before completion of its pillars. This is transmitted. Translation: If a traveler prayed four rak'ahs and sat in the second rak'ah to the extent of tashahhud, then the first two rak'ahs suffice for the fard and the last two are nafl for him, by analogy with Fajr. And he becomes sinful due to delaying the salutation. And if he did not sit in the second rak'ah to the extent of tashahhud, then this prayer is invalidated because the nafl became mixed with the fard before completing its pillars. Explanation: The issue is that a traveler prayed four rak'ahs instead of two, and he sat in the second rak'ah to the extent of tashahhud, so the first two count as fard and the last two as nafl. The author of Hidayah draws analogy with Fajr: if one prays four for Fajr and sits at the second, the Fajr fard is fulfilled. However, he is sinful for delaying the salutation. And if the traveler did not sit in the second rak'ah to the extent of tashahhud, his prayer becomes invalid. The reason is that the nafl is mixed with the fard before the completion of its pillars. The pillars are not complete because the last sitting is a pillar and was omitted. And mixing nafl with fard before completing the pillars of fard is an invalidator of prayer. Therefore his prayer is invalid.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on a traveler who mistakenly prays four rak'ahs (instead of two for qasr) and sits for tashahhud in the second rak'ah. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios: (1) If he sits in the second rak'ah for the duration of tashahhud, the first two rak'ahs count as the fard (obligatory) prayer, and the last two become nafl (voluntary). This is analogous to someone praying four rak'ahs for Fajr—the first two suffice for fard. However, he commits a sin by delaying the salutation (tashahhud of the second rak'ah is early, but after the fard is complete, he should have ended the prayer). (2) If he does not sit in the second rak'ah for tashahhud, the prayer is invalid (batil) because the nafil (the extra two rak'ahs) becomes mixed with the fard before its pillars are complete. The fard's pillars are incomplete because the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) is a pillar and is omitted. Mixing nafl with fard before the fard's completion invalidates the prayer. This ruling emphasizes the importance of completing the fard's pillars before adding nafl.

Key Terms
تشهد (tashahhud): The sitting for reciting the testimony of faith in the second/sitting rak'ah.
قعدہ اخیرہ (qa'dah akhirah): The final sitting in the last rak'ah of prayer; a pillar (rukn) in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a traveler prays 4 rak'ahs for Zuhr (intended qasr) and does NOT sit at the second rak'ah, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The first two rak'ahs count as fard, last two as nafl, and he is sinful.
B) The entire prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
C) The entire prayer is valid as a full 4-rak'ah prayer.
D) Only the last two rak'ahs count as fard.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a traveler's mistaken four-rak'ah prayer depends on whether he performed the second sitting; sitting completes the fard, not sitting invalidates it.

When Does Qasr Begin? Leaving the City Limits
Determining when the traveler begins to shorten prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a traveler begins qasr and explain the evidence from the athar of Ali and the hadith of Anas.

Core Idea
Qasr starts when the traveler physically leaves the city's built-up area, not before.

The question of when a traveler may shorten the prayer is critical for correct practice. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position that qasr becomes obligatory only upon leaving the actual houses and dwellings of the city. We will study the reasoning and the key proof texts from the Prophet's companions.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act (traveler's prayer) and the ruling (qasr becomes wajib upon leaving the city's houses).
The passage uses 'biyut al-misr' (houses of the city) to indicate the built-up area.
2
Identify the underlying principle
The ruling of travel attaches when leaving the city, just as the ruling of residence attaches when entering.
The author uses qiyas: as iqamah relates to entering, safar relates to leaving.
3
Analyze the athar of Ali
Examine the wording 'law jawazna hadha al-khuss la-qasarna' — leaving the huts triggers qasr.
'Khuss' refers to makeshift huts at the city boundary.
4
Analyze the hadith of Anas
The Prophet prayed Zuhr in Madinah (full) and Asr at Dhu'l-Hulayfah (shortened), indicating departure.
Dhu'l-Hulayfah is about 5 miles away, outside Madinah's limits.
5
Apply the rule to a modern scenario
A traveler must literally leave the last building of the city; being at the city limit gate is not enough.
In large cities, the 'built-up area' may extend; one leaves when the continuous buildings end.

Source Text

And when the traveler leaves the houses of the city, he prays two rak'ahs, because residence is related to entering them, so travel is related to leaving them. In this chapter there is an athar from Ali: 'If we pass beyond these huts, we shorten.' Translation: And when the traveler has left the houses of the city, he prays two rak'ahs, because the ruling of residence is connected to entering them, so the ruling of travel is connected to leaving them. And in this chapter there is an athar of Ali: 'If we go beyond these huts, we shorten.' Explanation: The question is: When does one start to qasr after beginning the journey? The ruling is that when he goes outside the inhabited area, qasr becomes wajib upon him. The proof is that when a traveler enters his home city's inhabited area, the ruling of residence applies, so when he leaves that area, the ruling of travel applies. Commentary
This passage explains when a traveler should begin to shorten prayer (qasr). The ruling is that he must actually leave the built-up area (houses, city limits) of his hometown. The reasoning is that the ruling of residence (iqamah) attaches when entering the city, so the ruling of travel attaches when leaving it. The author supports this with an athar (report) from Ali ibn Abi Talib and a hadith from Anas ibn Malik. The athar of Ali states: 'If we go beyond these huts (khuss), we shorten.' The word 'khuss' refers to makeshift huts. This indicates that leaving the actual dwellings constitutes the start of travel. The hadith of Anas shows that the Prophet prayed Zuhr with four rak'ahs in Madinah and then Asr at Dhu'l-Hulayfah (a place about 5 miles from Madinah) as two rak'ahs, indicating that once he was outside the city limits, he shortened. Therefore, for qasr to become applicable, the traveler must physically depart from the populated area of his city.

Key Terms
خص (khuss): A hut or makeshift dwelling made of bamboo or wood, referring to the city limits.
ذو الحليفة (Dhu'l-Hulayfah): A place about 5 miles from Madinah, the miqat for Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Qasr begins only when the traveler physically leaves the built-up area of the city, not upon intention or partial departure.

Duration of Stay to Become Muqim: 15 Days vs 4 Days
Hanafi and Shafi'i disagreement on minimum stay to be resident

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires a 15-day intention to become muqim and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using Quranic interpretation.

Core Idea
To become a resident (muqim), a traveler must intend to stay 15 days — the same duration as the period of purity (tuhr).

The distinction between a traveler (musafir) and a resident (muqim) determines whether one prays qasr or full prayers. But what minimum stay changes that status? The Hanafi school sets 15 days, while the Shafi'i school sets 4 days. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi proof and the inter-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate that according to the Hanafi school, a traveler becomes a muqim only if he intends to stay in a town or village for 15 days or more.
The text emphasizes intention (niyyah) of 15 days, not merely staying.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i (and Imam Malik) holds that intending 4 days (or staying more than 4 days) makes one a muqim.
There is also a narration from Shafi'i that even without intention, staying more than 4 days suffices.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i school argues from the Quranic verse 'When you travel in the land...' (4:101), interpreting that travel ends after a four-day stay.
The exact verse is not fully quoted in the text but is referenced.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school provides its own proof: analogy (qiyas) with the period of purity (tuhr), which is 15 days; further supported by athar (sayings) of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar, which in such matters carry weight comparable to hadith.
The Hanafi response rejects the Shafi'i interpretation as insufficiently grounded.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi, a traveler intending 4–14 days remains a musafir and prays qasr; under Shafi'i, he becomes muqim and must pray full prayers.
This impacts daily prayer obligations for travelers.

And he continues to be under the ruling of travel until he intends to reside in a town or village for fifteen days or more. If he intends less than that, he shortens, because it is necessary to consider a period. Since travel includes halting, we estimated it with the period of purity (tuhr), because both are periods that impose rulings. This is transmitted from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar, and an athar in such matters is like a hadith. The restriction to town or village indicates that intention of residence is not valid in a desert. That is apparent. Explanation: The issue is that the ruling of travel remains until he intends to stay in a town or village for fifteen days or more. When he intends fifteen days or more, the travel ruling ends and he is called a resident (muqim). If he intends less than that, he is not a resident according to us, but he will pray qasr. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i said that by intending four days he becomes a resident. One narration from Shafi'i is that when he stays more than four days, he becomes a resident whether he intends or not. The gist is that between us and Shafi'i there are two points of difference: one is the minimum number of days for becoming a muqim. According to us, by intending fifteen days he becomes muqim; according to them, by intending four days. Imam Shafi'i argues from the Quran: 'When you travel in the land...'
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage discusses the minimum duration of stay that changes a traveler's status to resident (muqim), affecting whether he must pray full prayers or can shorten. The Hanafi position is that one must intend to stay fifteen days or more in a town or village; otherwise, he remains a traveler and prays qasr. The period of fifteen days is established by qiyas (analogy) with the period of purity (tuhr, the menstrual clean period), as both are durations that trigger rulings. This is further supported by the statements of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar, which are given weight like hadith in such matters. The restriction to 'town or village' indicates that intending residence in a desert (uninhabited area) does not make one a muqim. In contrast, Imam Shafi'i holds that intending four days (or staying more than four days) makes one a muqim. He bases this on the Quranic verse 'When you travel in the land...' (which discusses qasr), interpreting that travel ends after a four-day stay. This is a significant inter-madhhab difference: the Hanafi minimum is 15 days, while the Shafi'i minimum is 4 days, with practical consequences for prayer obligations.

Key Terms
مقیم (muqim): A resident who is not a traveler; prays full prayer.
طهر (tuhr): The period of purity between menses, typically 15 days minimum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 3 days
B) 4 days
C) 15 days
D) 10 days

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uniquely sets 15 days as the minimum intention for residency (muqim), derived from analogy with the menstrual purity period (tuhr) and companion reports.

The Start of Qasr: Leaving Habitation
Ruling with proof on when qasr becomes operative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a traveler must begin shortening prayer and identify the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the Companions.

Core Idea
Qasr begins when the traveler leaves the built-up area of his town, not before.

This passage addresses the practical question of when a traveler must start shortening his prayers. The Hanafi school ties the ruling to the physical boundary of the inhabited area. The text provides two key pieces of evidence: the practice of Ali (RA) and the explicit action of the Prophet (SAW) at Dhu'l-Hulayfah. Let's examine how these establish the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling class
What is qasr? Shortening four-rak'ah prayers to two. The text says qasr becomes 'wajib' upon leaving the inhabited area. Note: Standard Hanafi classification considers qasr as sunnah mu'akkadah, not strictly wajib, but here 'wajib' means necessary in practice.
The text uses 'wajib' in the sense of a sunnah that must be observed.
2
Locate the boundary criterion
The trigger is leaving the 'inhabited area' (عمارت) of the hometown. This is defined by the last houses or buildings. The athar of Ali mentions 'reed huts' as a boundary marker.
Modern equivalent: the last building of the city limit.
3
Examine the evidence
The athar of Ali (RA) states: 'If we pass beyond these huts, we shorten prayer.' The hadith of Anas (RA) reports that the Prophet prayed Zuhr with 4 rak'ahs in Medina and Asr with 2 rak'ahs at Dhu'l-Hulayfah, demonstrating that qasr started after leaving the city.
Dhu'l-Hulayfah is about 10 km from Medina, an area with no buildings.
4
Distinguish the authority
The text explicitly says 'qasr becomes wajib'. However, the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that qasr is a sunnah mu'akkadah. The passage may be using 'wajib' in the sense of 'highly recommended' or 'necessary' for the traveler.
This nuance is important when comparing with other schools.
5
Apply to a real scenario
A traveler living in a city drives out. According to the Hanafi ruling, he should start qasr once he has passed the last house or building, not when he leaves his home door or when he crosses the city sign.
If the city is large with suburbs, one must reach the uninhabited area.

Chapter: Prayer of the Traveler. ... There is a relation to the ruling of travel, so it will be related to leaving these houses. In this chapter there is an athar of Ali (RA): If we pass beyond these huts, we pray qasr. Explanation: The question is when to start qasr after beginning travel. The ruling is: when he comes out of the inhabited area, qasr becomes wajib upon him. The proof is that when a traveler enters his home city's inhabited area, the ruling of residence applies; so when he leaves it, the ruling of travel applies. Commentary
This passage states the ruling on when a traveler begins to shorten prayer. The text explains that qasr becomes obligatory once the traveler leaves the inhabited area of his hometown. The proof is provided from an athar of Ali (RA) that if they pass beyond the reed huts, they should shorten prayer. This is further supported by a hadith of Anas (RA) that the Prophet (SAW) prayed Zuhr with four rak'ahs in Medina and Asr with two rak'ahs at Dhu'l-Hulayfah, which is a place outside Medina. The underlying principle is that the rulings of travel and residence are tied to being inside or outside the city boundaries.

Key Terms
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rak'ah prayers to two rak'ahs for a traveler.
سفر (safar): Travel, specifically a journey of three days and nights (approx. 48 miles) according to Hanafi.
اثر (athar): A saying or practice of a Companion of the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) After traveling three days.
D) After reaching his destination.

Key Takeaway
Qasr begins after leaving the inhabited area, demonstrated by the Prophet's action at Dhu'l-Hulayfah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
The Hanafi Ruling on the Minimum Period of Residence (Iqamah)
Establishing the minimum period of residence (15 days) to become a muqim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for when a traveler becomes a muqim and explain the qiyas to the period of purity (tuhr) as evidence.

Core Idea
A traveler becomes a muqim by intending 15 days' residence – analogized to the 15-day minimum purity period.

How long must a traveler intend to stay in a place before he loses the allowance to shorten prayers? The Hanafi school sets this threshold at 15 days, drawing an analogy to the period of purity (tuhr) from menstruation. This lesson unpacks that ruling, the evidence behind it, and the conditions attached: intention and location in a town or village.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules on the traveler (musafir) who intends to stay in a place. Determine when he becomes a muqim (resident) and must pray full prayers instead of qasr.
The ruling is not about the permissibility of qasr itself, but about the legal status change.
2
Locate the dalil (proof) for the 15-day period
The text cites two sources: (1) qiyas to the minimum purity period (tuhr) of 15 days, and (2) athar (reports) from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. Understand why both are used.
The qiyas is based on the shared quality of being 'periods that cause obligations to return' (e.g., prayer after menstruation, full prayer after travel).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
Explain the analogy: Just as the minimum tuhr is 15 days and it restores the obligation of prayer, so too the minimum iqamah is 15 days and it restores the obligation of full prayer. Also note that the athar of the Companions is treated like a hadith in shariah-estimated matters (ma la yu'qal).
This highlights the Hanafi method of using qiyas and accepting Companion statements as proof when they deal with matters beyond rational determination.
4
Identify conditions for the ruling to apply
Two conditions are explicit: (1) the traveler must intend (niyyah) residence for 15 days or more; (2) the residence must be in a town (balda) or village (qarya), not in a wilderness (mafazah).
If intention is less than 15 days, the traveler remains on the ruling of travel and continues qasr.
5
Note the reliance on Zahir al-Riwayah and the mufta bihi
The text affirms that this is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah and that the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the 15-day rule with intention. Be aware of an incomplete mention of Qadi Abu Yusuf's view about shepherds.
This lesson focuses on the established school position; the intra-madhhab difference will be noted but not fully resolved.

ابوالحسن قدوری کا اقامت کے لئے بلدہ یا قریہ کی قید لگانا اس طرف مشیر ہے کہ جنگل میں اقامت کی نیت کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ یہی ظاہر الروایۃ ہے۔ اگر چہ قاضی ابو یوسف نے فرمایا ہے کہ چرواہے اگر گھاس پانی کی He remains under the ruling of travel until he intends residence in a town or village for fifteen days or more. If he intends less than that, he shortens, because a period must be considered for residence, since travel accommodates staying. So we analogized it to the period of purity (tuhr), because both are periods that are causative. This is transmitted from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. The athar in such matters is like the hadith. The restriction to town and village indicates that intending residence in a wilderness is not valid, and this is apparent. ... The explanation: He will remain under the ruling of travel until he intends residence in a city or village for fifteen days or more. If he intends less, he shortens because residence requires a period. Because travel also includes staying, we measured the period of residence by the period of purity, because both are periods that cause obligations. This amount is narrated from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. And in such a chapter, the statement of a Companion is like the statement of the Messenger of Allah (SAW). The restriction to city and village indicates that intending residence in a wilderness is not correct; this is apparent. ... Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i said that with the intention of staying four days, one becomes a resident. Shafi'i has a statement that when one stays more than four days, he becomes a resident, whether he intends or not. So between us and Shafi'i there are two points of difference. First, the minimum period required to become a resident: according to us, with the intention of fifteen days; according to them, with the intention of four days. Shafi'i argues from the Quran: 'When you travel in the land, there is no blame on you to shorten prayer.' The opposite implication is that if there is no travel, qasr is not permissible. So when the traveler intends residence, he abandons travel, and then qasr is not permissible. But there is an objection: if he intends less than four days, also there is no travel. The answer is that the text requires that less than four days also qasr should not be allowed, but we abandon the text in the case of less than four days due to consensus (ijma), because no one says that such a short stay makes one a resident. ... The second difference is about intention. According to us, intention is a condition for residence; so without intention, even if he stays fifteen days, he is not a resident. According to Shafi'i, intention is not a condition. His proof is the saying of Uthman: 'Whoever stays four days, he prays full prayer,' without mentioning intention. The Hanafi proof: The traveler does not necessarily travel 24 hours a day; he also stops. So travel and staying coexist. To distinguish, a period is needed. So we analogize to the period of purity (tuhr), which is 15 days. The authority: Saheb Hidayah says that the determination of 15 days is among the shariah-estimated matters. And in matters not understood by intellect, the athar of a Companion is like a hadith. Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar are reported to have said that if you enter a town with intention to stay 15 days, complete your prayer; if you do not know when you will depart, shorten. Qadi Abu Yusuf said that shepherds, if they pitch tents in a place of grass and water... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage discusses the threshold for a traveler to become a resident (muqim) and the disputes with other schools. The Hanafi position is that a traveler remains on the ruling of travel until he intends to reside in a town or village for 15 days or more. If he intends less, he continues to shorten prayer. This is based on qiyas to the minimum period of purity (tuhr) from menstruation, which is 15 days, because both are periods that cause obligations to return (e.g., prayer after menstruation, full prayer after travel). Evidence is also drawn from the statements of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar, which are treated like hadith in such matters. The text then addresses two disputes with Imam Shafi'i: (1) the minimum period: Shafi'i says 4 days, relying on the opposite implication of the Quranic verse (that qasr is only for travel) and the statement of Uthman; (2) intention: Shafi'i does not require intention. The Hanafi response uses qiyas and the need for a distinct period. The passage also notes that the specification of a town or village is necessary; intending residence in a wilderness is invalid. Finally, there is a reference to a view of Qadi Abu Yusuf regarding shepherds, but the text is cut off.

Key Terms
اقامت (iqamah): Residence, staying in a place with the intention of becoming a resident (muqim).
نیت (niyyah): Intention to reside, considered a condition for becoming a muqim in Hanafi.
طہر (tuhr): The period of purity between menstrual cycles, minimum 15 days in Hanafi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum number of days a traveler must intend to reside in a town or village to become a muqim?
A) 4 days
B) 10 days
C) 15 days
D) 20 days

Key Takeaway
A traveler becomes a muqim by intending 15 days' residence in a town/village; intention and location are crucial conditions.

Salah — Prayer

The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Iqamah: Minimum Period and Intention
Refuting Shafi'i's view on iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two points of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding iqamah and evaluate each side's proofs.

Core Idea
Hanafi requires 15 days intended residence with intention; Shafi'i requires 4 days without intention.

The traveler's status is contested between schools: how many days of intended stay turn a musafir into a muqim? And is intention necessary? This lesson examines the two disputes between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Shafi'i, their proofs, and the Hanafi responses. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to weigh evidence from Quran, hadith, qiyas, and ijma.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two disputed issues
The text explicitly lists two disagreements: (1) the minimum period of intended residence to become a muqim, and (2) whether intention (niyyah) is a condition for becoming a muqim.
These are separate but related; the former deals with duration, the latter with volition.
2
State the Shafi'i position and their proofs
Shafi'i says 4 days of intended stay suffice, and intention is not required. His proofs: (a) opposite implication of Quran 4:101 (qasr only for travel), (b) the saying of Uthman: 'Whoever stays four days prays full' without mentioning intention.
The text also mentions Imam Malik agreeing with Shafi'i.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to each proof
For the Quranic opposite implication: Hanafi argues it would also forbid qasr for stays less than 4 days, but this is rejected by ijma (consensus). Therefore the text is abandoned in that case, and analogy (qiyas) is used instead. For Uthman's saying: it does not explicitly negate intention, and the Hanafi school supports intention with qiyas and the athar of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar.
The Hanafi reliance on ijma as a mukhassis (specifier) is a key usul point.
4
Examine the Hanafi positive proofs for their positions
For the 15-day period: qiyas to the minimum tuhr (15 days), and the athar of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. For intention: logical argument that residence is a legal concept requiring a deliberate change of status; also supported by the athar of Ibn Abbas ('if you intend to stay 15 days, complete prayer') which implies intention.
The athar is treated as equivalent to hadith in shariah-estimated matters (ma la yu'qal).
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Take a concrete case: a traveler intends 10 days. Under Hanafi, he remains musafir (shortens). Under Shafi'i, he becomes muqim (prays full) because 10 > 4 days. Moreover, if he stays 4 days without intention, Shafi'i considers him muqim; Hanafi does not.
This shows the real impact of the ikhtilaf on daily worship.

مقیم بننے کے لئے کتنے دن کی اقامت کی نیت ضروری ہے
ولايزال على حكم السفر حتى ينوى الاقامة في بلدة او قرية خمسة عشر يوما او اكثر وان نوى اقل من ذلك قصر لانه لابد من اعتبار مدة لان السفر يجامعه اللبث فقدرناها بمدة الطهر لانهما مدتان موجبتان وهو ماثور عن ابن عباس وابن عمر والاثر فى مثله كالخبر والتقييد بالبلدة والقرية يشير الى انه لاتصح نية الإقامة في المفازة وهو الظاهر

زجمہ اور سفر کے حکم پر ہمیشہ باقی رہے گا یہاں تک کہ کسی شہر یا گاؤں میں پندرہ دن یا اس سے زیادہ قیام کی نیت کرے۔ اور اگر اس سے کم کی نیت کی تو قصر کرے کیونکہ قیام کے اندر مدت کا اعتبار کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اس لئے کہ سفر کے اندر بھی ٹھہراؤ موجود ہوتا ہے پس ہم نے مدت اقامت کا مدت طہر کے ساتھ اندازہ کیا کیونکہ یہ دونوں مدتیں واجب کرنے والی ہیں۔ اور یہی مقدار ابن عباس اور ابن عمر سے منقول ہے۔ اور اس جیسے باب میں صحابی کا قول رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول کے مانند ہوتا ہے شہر اور گاؤں کی قید لگانا اس بات کی طرف اشارہ کرتا ہے کہ جنگل کے اندرا قامت کی نیت کر نا صحیح نہیں ہے یہی ظاہر ہے۔ کیا تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ سفر کا حکم اس وقت باقی رہے گا جب تک کہ کسی شہر یا گاؤں میں پندرہ دن یا اس سے زیادہ قیام کی نیت نہ کرے پس جب پندرہ دن یا اس سے زیادہ کے قیام کی نیت کرے گا تو سفر کا حکم ختم ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ شخص مقیم کہلائے گا۔ اور اگر پندرہ ان سے کم مظہر نے کی نیت کی تو ہمارے نزدیک شخص مقیم نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ قصر نماز پڑھے گا۔
حضرت امام مالک اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ چار دن قیام کی نیت سے مقیم ہو جائے گا۔ امام شافعی کا ایک قول یہ ہے کہ جب چار دن سے زائد قیام کیا تو یہ مقیم ہو گیا۔ خواہ نیت کرے یا نیت نہ کرے حاصل یہ کہ ہمارے اور امام شافعی کی درمیان دو جگہ اختلاف ہے۔ ایک یہ کہ مقیم ہونے کے لئے کم از کم کتنے دن کے قیام کی نیت ضروری ہے سو ہمارے نزدیک پندرہ دن کی نیت سے مقیم ہو جائے گا۔ اور ان کے نزدیک چار ان کی نیت سے مقیم ہو جائے گا۔ امام شافعی نے اپنے اس قول پر قرآن سے استدلال کیا ہے ارشاد خداوندی ہے إِذَا ضَرَ بُتُم فِى

باب صلوة المسافر
۲۸۲
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم الْأَرْضِ فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ اَنْ تَقْصُرُوا مِنَ الصَّلوةِ اس آیت میں اللہ تعالیٰ نے ضرب فی الارض یعنی چلنے سے قصر کو مباح کیا ہے اس کا مفہوم مخالف یہی کہ اگر ضرب فی الارض نہ ہو تو قصر مباح نہیں ہے پس جب مسافر نے اقامت کی نیت کی تو اس نے ضرب فی الارض کو چھوڑ دیا۔ اور جب ضرب فی الارض کو چھوڑ دیا تو اس کے واسطے قصر کرنا مباح نہ رہا لیکن اس پر سوال ہوگا کہ اگر چار دن سے کم قیام کی نیت کرے تو بھی قصر کرنے کی اجازت نہ ہونی چاہئے کیونکہ ضرب فی الارض اس صورت میں بھی نہیں پایا گیا۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ نص کا تقاضا تو یہی ہے کہ چار دن سے کم قیام کرنے سے قصر کا حکم باقی نہ رہے۔ مگر ہم نے دلیل اجتماع کی وجہ سے چار دن سے کم میں اس نص کو ترک کر دیا ہے اس لئے کہ اس س کم قیام کی نیت سے مقیم ہونے کا کوئی قائل نہیں ہے۔
اقامت کے لئے نیت شرط ہے دوسرا اختلاف یہ ہے کہ اقامت کے لئے ہمارے نزدیک اصل نیست شرط ہے چنانچہ ہمارے نزد یک بلانیت اقامت مقیم نہیں ہوگا۔ خواہ پندرہ دن سے زائد قیام کرے۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک مقیم ہونے کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل حضرت عثمان کا قول من اقام اربعا اہم ہے یعنی جو شخص چار دن قیام کرے وہ پوری نماز پڑھے اس قول میں نیت کا ذکر نہیں ہے لہذا ثابت ہوا کہ مقیم ہونے کے لئے نیت کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اقامت کے لئے پندرہ یوم کا اعتبار کرنے میں امام اعظم کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مسافر کے لئے یہ ضروری نہیں ہے کہ وہ شب وروز ۲۴ گھنٹے چلتا ر ہے۔ بلکہ وہ بسا اوقات ٹھہرتا بھی ہے اور کافی دیر تک ٹھہر جاتا ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ سفر اور لبث ( ٹھہرنا دونوں جمع ہو جاتے ہیں۔ یہ بات بھی اظہر من الشمس ہے کہ ٹھہرنے کا نام ہی اقامت اور مقیم ہونا ہے پس چونکہ ان دونوں کے درمیان فرق کرنے کے لئے ایک مدت کا اعتبار کرنا ضروری ہے۔ اس لئے ہم نے مدت طہر پر قیاس کر کے مدت اقامت پندرہ یوم مقرر کی ہے۔ رہی بات یہ کہ قیاس کی علت مشترک کیا ہے۔ سو اس بارے میں صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ مدت طہر اور مدت اقامت دونوں کا موجب ہونا علت مشترکہ ہے۔ یعنی حیض کی وجہ سے جو عبادت ساقط ہوگئی تھی مدت طہر کی وجہ سے جس طرح وہ عود کر آتی ہے اس طرح سفر کی وجہ سے ساقط شدہ عبادت بھی مدت اقامت کی وجہ سے عود کر آتی ہے پس اس قیاس کی بنیاد پر جس طرح ادنی مدت طہر پندرہ دن ہیں اسی طرح ادنی مدت اقامت بھی پندرہ یوم ہوں گے ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ طہر کی ضد حیض کی ادنیٰ مدت تین دن ہیں۔ تو اقامت کی ضد سفر کی ادنی مدت بھی تین دن ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مدت اقامت کا پندرہ دن ہونا حضرت ابن عباس اور حضرت ابن عمر رضی اللہ عنہم سے بھی مروی ہے۔ چنانچہ مجاہد نے روایت کی ہے عن ابن عباس وابن عمر رضى الله عنهما قالا اذا دخلت بلدة وانت مسافر وفي عزمک ان تقيم بها خمسة عشر يوما فاكمل الصلوة وان كنت لاتدرى متى تظعن فاقصر یعنی ان دونوں حضرات صحابہ نے فرمایا کہ جب تو کسی شہر میں داخل ہو۔ حالانکہ تو مسافر ہے۔ اور تیرا ارادہ پندرہ دن قیام کا ہے تو نماز پوری پڑھ اور اگر تجھ کو یعلم نہیں کہ کب سفر کرے گا تو تو قصر کرتا رہ ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ پندرہ دن کی تحدید مقدرات شرعیہ میں سے ہے اور ایام کی تقدیر وتحدید ایسی چیز ہے جس کی طرف عقل بھی راہ یاب نہیں ہے۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ مالا يعقل کے اندر اثر صحابی بمنزلہ خبر اور حدیث کے ہوتا ہے۔ گویا ابن عباس اور ابن عمر نے پندرہ یوم کی تحسین حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے سن کر بیان کی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ امام ابوالحسن قدوری کا اقامت کے لئے بلدہ یا قریہ کی قید لگانا اس طرف مشیر ہے کہ جنگل میں اقامت کی نیت کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ یہی ظاہر الروایۃ ہے۔ اگر چہ قاضی ابو یوسف نے فرمایا ہے کہ چرواہے اگر گھاس پانی کی جگہ خیمہ زن ہو جائیں
He remains under the ruling of travel until he intends residence in a town or village for fifteen days or more. If he intends less than that, he shortens, because a period must be considered for residence, since travel accommodates staying. So we analogized it to the period of purity (tuhr), because both are periods that are causative. This is transmitted from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. The athar in such matters is like the hadith. The restriction to town and village indicates that intending residence in a wilderness is not valid, and this is apparent. ... The explanation: He will remain under the ruling of travel until he intends residence in a city or village for fifteen days or more. If he intends less, he shortens because residence requires a period. Because travel also includes staying, we measured the period of residence by the period of purity, because both are periods that cause obligations. This amount is narrated from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar. And in such a chapter, the statement of a Companion is like the statement of the Messenger of Allah (SAW). The restriction to city and village indicates that intending residence in a wilderness is not correct; this is apparent. ... Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i said that with the intention of staying four days, one becomes a resident. Shafi'i has a statement that when one stays more than four days, he becomes a resident, whether he intends or not. So between us and Shafi'i there are two points of difference. First, the minimum period required to become a resident: according to us, with the intention of fifteen days; according to them, with the intention of four days. Shafi'i argues from the Quran: 'When you travel in the land, there is no blame on you to shorten prayer.' The opposite implication is that if there is no travel, qasr is not permissible. So when the traveler intends residence, he abandons travel, and then qasr is not permissible. But there is an objection: if he intends less than four days, also there is no travel. The answer is that the text requires that less than four days also qasr should not be allowed, but we abandon the text in the case of less than four days due to consensus (ijma), because no one says that such a short stay makes one a resident. ... The second difference is about intention. According to us, intention is a condition for residence; so without intention, even if he stays fifteen days, he is not a resident. According to Shafi'i, intention is not a condition. His proof is the saying of Uthman: 'Whoever stays four days, he prays full prayer,' without mentioning intention. The Hanafi proof: The traveler does not necessarily travel 24 hours a day; he also stops. So travel and staying coexist. To distinguish, a period is needed. So we analogize to the period of purity (tuhr), which is 15 days. The authority: Saheb Hidayah says that the determination of 15 days is among the shariah-estimated matters. And in matters not understood by intellect, the athar of a Companion is like a hadith. Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar are reported to have said that if you enter a town with intention to stay 15 days, complete your prayer; if you do not know when you will depart, shorten. Qadi Abu Yusuf said that shepherds, if they pitch tents in a place of grass and water... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage discusses the threshold for a traveler to become a resident (muqim) and the disputes with other schools. The Hanafi position is that a traveler remains on the ruling of travel until he intends to reside in a town or village for 15 days or more. If he intends less, he continues to shorten prayer. This is based on qiyas to the minimum period of purity (tuhr) from menstruation, which is 15 days, because both are periods that cause obligations to return (e.g., prayer after menstruation, full prayer after travel). Evidence is also drawn from the statements of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar, which are treated like hadith in such matters. The text then addresses two disputes with Imam Shafi'i: (1) the minimum period: Shafi'i says 4 days, relying on the opposite implication of the Quranic verse (that qasr is only for travel) and the statement of Uthman; (2) intention: Shafi'i does not require intention. The Hanafi response uses qiyas and the need for a distinct period. The passage also notes that the specification of a town or village is necessary; intending residence in a wilderness is invalid. Finally, there is a reference to a view of Qadi Abu Yusuf regarding shepherds, but the text is cut off.

Key Terms
اقامت (iqamah): Residence, staying in a place with the intention of becoming a resident (muqim).
مفہوم مخالف (mafhum al-mukhalafah): Opposite implication; a linguistic inference that the opposite of the stated condition holds the opposite ruling.
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of the scholars; used here to restrict the apparent meaning of the Quranic verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which school of thought does NOT require intention (niyyah) to become a muqim?
A) Hanafi
B) Shafi'i
C) Both require it
D) Neither requires it

Key Takeaway
Hanafi and Shafi'i differ on both the minimum period (15 vs 4 days) and the necessity of intention for becoming a muqim.
